1. EXCELLENCE 
1.0. THE PROBLEM, THE NEED AND THE OPPORTUNITY. 
“We all die, but looking” is the title of the autobiography of Alberto García Alix, one of the most representat ive 
photographers of 2nd half of 20th Century in Europe. It is impossible summarize better, in a few words, the relevance 
of the natural capability of human being of catching everything that surrounds him.  
The human flair of converting images into memorie s contribute on building w hat we were, what we are and surely 
what we will be. Since last 1895 the memories of history of human being ha s being helped by the possibility of 
capturing and saving this part of our evolution into photographs and movies. These physical supports have sav ed 
main part of our global cultural, social and p olitical history. But, looking into each individual, also gav e the 
possibility of recording part of our family heritage. 
Photographs and movies  have helped to preserve the cultural material that is faithful witness of socio -cultural 
European evolution in t he recent era. It encompasses not only the possibility to und erstand the development of new 
arts such as cinema, photog raphy or graphic arts but also the preservation of the socio -cultural memories of citizens 
in major museums, local museums (real testimon y of the history of cities and their people) located in many towns 
worldwide & in a huge number of private collections.  
A huge percentage of the recent European cultural heritage ( CH) can be found in movies , photographs, posters and 
slides produced between 1895 to nowadays were made using cellulose derivatives. More than 75 years of visual and 
audio memories are up to now  in serious danger to be lost due to the natural instabil ity cellulose acetate (CA) and 
cellulose nitrate (CN) materials. The worldwide estimation of such holdings within professional film archives is 
around 18 Mio of film reels on cellulose acetate, where of ca. 5% are in a critical stage or showing signs of 
vinegar syndrome (survey carried out by the OEAW -PhA in 2012, performed with 20 ins titutions, extrapolated to 
125 members of FIAF (Fédération Internationale des Archives du Film). Figure 1.1.a shows an example of such film. 
There have had other technical approaches to solve this real problem that follow the line of replication and copy t he 
original ones in modern digital supports  (for example PIQLBox©- www.piql.com/). But, they do  not give the 
possibility of a real preservation of the original ones. In the actual t echnology age, our duty,  with the people that 
preceded us, pass through help on the preservation of these parts of original memories that built our past history and 
will help on understanding our future. 
Under the technical point of view, conservators cons ider two approaches 
when p lanning treatments to extend the useful lifetime of cultural 
materials: preventive or passive and active or interventive. However in the 
case of cellulose derivat ives and other components of the movie or 
photography, once initiated, degradation cannot be p revented, reversed or 
stopped, but only inhibited or slowed. Inhibitive conservation of cellulose 
derivatives can either involve the removal or reduction of factors cau sing 
degradation including light, oxygen, acids, fungus and re lative humidity, 
or of any  breakdown products which accelerate degradation,  as well as 
cost-sensitive processes such as freeze. The cell ulose derivative 
degradations is autocatalytic increasing constantly the level of 
degradation with the time.  
 
Figure 1.1.a Cellulose nitrate film under 
an autocatalytic degradation process 
induces by moisture and acid off-gassing. 
The storage and the pr eservation of the cultural heritage made on cellulose ethe r or ester –and derivatives- are an 
important issue for the in novation and creativeness of future generations. The degradation of this ma terial is 
significant, fast, and results in the loss of infor mation and values. Some of the main by -products of this pr ocess can 
be acetic acid (AA), nitric oxide (NO), and others. Different solution preservation approaches related to zeolites or 
active carbon adsorbers are well-known. Not only known are the chemica l reactions responsible of degradation (due 
to intrinsic nature of materials), but also the biological processes due to moulds development that spread quickly on 
the gelatin layer. So far we don’t have any easy system to treat moulded audio-visual materials. 
NEMOSINE aims to improve the traditional storage soluti ons, such as freeze storage (below 5ºC), by developing 
an innovative smart package  with the main goal of energy saving and extent conserv ation time of cultural 
objects based on cellulose derivat ives. Beyond the state of the art NEMOSINE plans to develop th e following 
modular and integrated products: i)High O2 barrier and Active packaging using non-odour additives, ii)Active acid 
adsorbers b ased on functionalized Metal Organic Framework (MOFs) integra ted in low density and porous 
structures, iii)Gas detection sensors based on nanotechnology to monitoring AA, water, O 2 & NO, iv) Multi -scale 
modelling to correlate degradation & sensors signals for maintenance prediction and integrate all these technologies 
in v)Packaging with modular design to fulfil the technical & economical requirements of the different CH made by 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 4 of 110 
cellulose derivatives and vi) Curative packages contain ing controlled release of natural antifungal additives. The 
main targets of NEMOSINE project are cellulose derivatives, from photographic, movies and audio substrates. 
The modular solution is one of main a dvantages of the innovativ e package. This design will allow to provide 
different versions of the product with more or less technology in cluded in the solution : PROTECTIVE (basic and 
premium mode l), and CURATIVE  (for damaged products) . In this way, the smar t package can be adapted t o 
different type of final clients –private collector, national museum s, regional collections,  councils and in stitutions, 
schools-, in terms of necessities, balancing re al value of the content and the package cost. The main project  
proposed modular innovations are summarized in figure 1.1.b: 
 
Figure 1.1.b. Scheme of the main innovations proposed in NEMOSINE project. 
In despite of problems of conservation of these materia ls, the European funded R&D projects dedicated to the 
preservation of the European Cultural Heritage have been always focused on the preservation of traditional fine arts 
as architecture, sculpture or painting (such as  NMP H2020 NANOCATHEDRAL or NANORESTART). NEMOSINE 
is the first one that will work on the preservation of the most recent ones, the photography & the cinema. 
1.1. OBJECTIVES 
The main objectives and their means of verification  of NEMOSINE pro ject, defined according to SMART 
principle (i.e. Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Responsible-Partner, Time-lined) are described in table 1.1.a 
Table 1.1.a. Main objectives of NEMOSINE project, potential exploitable results and partners involved and timin g. 
Objective 1:  Preparation of MOFs for the capture of AA in the presence of humidity with a n AA/Water 
selectivity above  three times above common adsorbents (i.e. activated carbons and zeolites).  Selected MOFs 
must be suitable to be incorporated into open cell foams or electrospinning nanofibers. Adsorption regeneration 
will be evaluated by the colour change of the carriers (Linked to WP2 & WP3). 
Structural and chemical characterization of select ive MOFs after synthesis and further s cale-up to reach TRL 
objective and evaluation of the removal efficiency of AA (kinetic profiles) from air with the developed materials 
in contr olled laboratory condition s. Incorporation in polymeric foams cells or nano fibres containing up to 
30%w/w of MOFs with a specific surface area between 5 to 10 km2/dm3. Performance indicators: by M18 and 
M30, a report will be prepared, that will include the fabrication of two generation of MOFs, By M38, a report of 
AA adsorption behaviour of MOF/foam or nanofibres materials will be prepared and  By M42, MOF/foams will 
be incorporated in the final packages and validated . Main Partners Involved : CNRS, PROM, MODISPREM,

and nanofibers with controlled release for artefacts protection against fungus to develop curative packages (linked 
to WP2 & WP3). 
Incorporation of selected antifungals in polymeric f oams and nanofibres with high specific surface to kill the 
fungal in films or photographs with medium or severe action of fungus. The possibility to have a package with 
control release fungal based on encapsulation technologies could allow a direct intervention optimizing the doses 
of antifungals, avoiding high expense s and time co nsumption. Monitoring control of the growth o f fungal 
(mainly aspergilius, clodosporium and penicillium spe cies). Performance indicators: by M 18, a report about 
the selection of best antifungal additive for CH protection, by M38, evaluate the  effectiveness of systems based

NPH and AIMPLAS 
Objective 3: To develop an integrated sensor fo r AA, NO & O 2 detection with a range of detection 25, 10 
&15 ppb respectively and a cost lower than 5 €/unit (Linked to WP4). 
Multi-sensor devices based on nanomaterials will be develop. Sensoring capabilities monitoring of selected 
sensors through suitable simulants, checking lower detection levels. Estimation of sensor costs at in dustrial 
production framework. Performance indicators: By M26 Functionalized sensor will be  ready to measure,  by 
M30, a report will be prepared with the results of high sensor sensitivity to gases involved in the cellulose 
derivatives degradation by M44 and M48, the sensors wil l be installed and validated in the premium package. 
Main Partners Involved; BIOSENSOR, NPH 
Objective 4: To develop multi-scale chemometric models to correlate sensors’ signals integrated in the 
package with degradation level of any type of cellulose derivatives CH artefacts (Linked to WP5). 
Hybrid models are the key for an accurate estimation of the evolution of degradation over time and a useful tool 
to design a personalized predictive maintenance . Performance indicators: by M 42, report will be prepared  
based on the optimization of simula tion software about degradation process . Main Partners Involved ; NOVA, 
IST & IRIS 
Objective 5: To equip the packaging with a Radio -frequency identification (RFID) function for the remote 
tracking of the integrated sensors and predicted degradation modules (linked to WP5). 
A tailored receiver for a quick centralised periodic review of the collection and its software embedding the 
predictive maintenance models will be delivered to inform to the conserver when actions  need to be 
implemented. A control platf orm will be developed to achieve this objective.  Performance indicators: by 
M32, a report will be prepared and will include some captures of control platform behaviour  by M44 and M48, 
the full control system will be  installed and validated in the premium package. Main Partners Involved ; IRIS, 
NOVA, IST. 
Objective 6: To design a cost-competitive plastic package with excellent water and oxygen barrier 
properties (less than 0.5 cm3/package day measured according ISO 15105-2 standard) (Linked to WP6). 
Selection of suitable barrier polymeric materials, optimization of multi-layer injection  process and appealing 
design to reach desired propertie s. Performance indicators: by M 30, a report will be prepared to  describe the 
barrier properties achieved by the multi layer polymeric package , by M44, the best polymeric materials will be 
used in the NEMOSINE’s package. Main Partners Involved AIMPLAS, AKUMPLAST & IPC. 
Objective 7: Smart package for cellulose based cultural heritage protection or curative performance must 
be designed according to modularity principles (Linked to WP1 and WP6). 
Modular design to provide different models including only a few or all proposed functionalities, from low cost 
to expensive packages with the objective to impact in a broad range of final users (professionals and particulars). 
Clear differentiation between properties, limitations of each designed model, perfectly oriented to real demands 
of the different kind of clients to reach the maximum co mmercial impact. The physical supports for  absorbers 
and antifungals will be designed to easy removal and replace when the sensors detects (or color change) that 
both system are collapsed. Foams and fibres will be full recyclable. Regeneration of MOFs will  be stud ied. 
Performance indicators: by M9 a preliminary 3D package concept will be proposed , by M24, a report will be 
prepared to  demonstrate the easy removal and change of the different technologic elements integrated in the 
active package. Main Partners Involved AIMPLAS, AKUMPLAST & IPC. 
Objective 8: Construction of three packages prototypes for selected applications (with different 
functionalities and target customers: protective (basic & premium) and curative (section 1.3.1) (Linked WP6).

stronger links within the consortium.  In that way, the well balanced expertise of the Consortium, added to the 
Implementation Plan help on ensuring that the partnership can achieve the specific objectives described.

is to have all the tools to initiate the degradation as NEMOSINE proposed or 
well to use a cura tive package that destroy the microorganism that initiate the 
vinegar syndrome.

expected to ensure long term protection 
and security of cultural heritage artefacts, 
taking i nto account  environmental and 
human risk factors.

extend its life expectancy by adsorbing off -gassing harmful chemicals, but also 
protect people from breathing acidic gases or man ipulate obj ects acid 
impregnated. Furthermore, the curative smart package will destroy the fungus 
by themselves (controlled release) avoiding the direct contact with the 
pathogens or the synthetic antifungals by the conservation employees.

solutions in the conservation of cul tural 
assets is expected.

long-term physical preservation of cultural heritage. Their induced effects are 
translated into improved pro cess effici ency of safeguarding heritage by

interventions and less associated costs  (estimated reduction around 50% of

1.3. CONCEPT AND METHODOLOGY 
1.3.1. Overall concept. 
NEMOSINE aims to develop 
modular and adaptable 
innovative smart packages to 
protect from audivisual 
cultural h eritage based on 
cellulose derivatives The 
modular concept of a whole 
protective device would allow 
to generate three different 
packages with different 
funtionalities and final cost, 
depending on the technical 
protective/ p reventive or 
curative purposes of  cultural 
objects (see figure 1.3.a). 
  
Figure 1.3.a. Scheme of three modular SMART package solutions. 
All the individual elements will be integrated 
in a smart package depending on the CH 
artefact deterioration grade and  other 
requirements for protectiv e or curative 
purposes. The basic design of this package (for 
the case of movies) is presented in figure 
1.3.b: 
 
 
 
 
Figure 1.3.b. Scheme of modular SMART 
package. 
 
These levels of technology would be based on the following approaches: 
1. Working on innovative and new acetic adsorbers based on hydrophobic MOFs with high specific surface 
and porosity  supported in different substrates , with high specific surface  and porosity  such as open cell 
foams and electros pinning nanofibers, as well as cellulose based on pa per or matt board due its excellent 
properties as absorber, recyclability and limited cost.  Paper or board ones will be produced in a renewable and 
low acetic acid barrier material. The physical supports for ads orbers and antifungals will be designed for e asy 
removal and replacement when the sensors detect that are exhausted. Foams and fibres will be fully 
recyclable and reusable. Saturation level of foams and nanofibres will be studied to determinate the durability 
and the necessities to change the adsorpt ion modular panel. Visual colour changes will be proposed for Basic 
preventive package users. In the case of PREMIUM model the control platform will determinate the clogging 
and the adsorption panel change deadl ine. The BASIC model will need a color change  indicator based on pH 
acidification. Reusability of the same panel after thermal treatments will be evaluated. 
2. To design high oxygen and moisture barrier injected packages  by combining different plastic materia ls 
with different barrier properties in non-conventional processes such as co-injection, over-moulding or in-mould 
labelling. Materials selected are suitable to be used in the protection of museum artefacts 2, these will include 
thermoplastic materials, coatings and aluminium foils in order to maximize the barrier properties, minimize the 
cost and to allow a easy recyclability. 
3. Active packaging for releasing non-aggressive active substances and moisture adsorbents to minimize the 
growing of fungus  such as nanoparticles and antifungal peptides. Despite the limitations to use chemicals in 
conservation, active packaging could be interesting to store artefacts (and stop further fungal development) and 
possibly to inhibit growths. In this sense, NEMOSINE project will develop two types of dispositives:  
 
 
2 www.morana-rtd.com/e-preservationscience/2010/Bergmair-04-06-2008.pdf 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 10 of 110 
a. Long-term protection, where using antifungal additives are controversial. The current tendency is to control 
the causes beyond the consequences maintaining the moisture content in a safe level. In this way, specific 
MOFs, zeolites, nanoclays or hydrophilic nanosilicas will be introduced in the foams and nanofibers to dry 
the atmosphere of package. 
b. Curative treatment as a kind of “on -field disinfection package”,  when the artefacts or objects are 
contaminated by the mic roorganisms, bacteries or fungus. This is not  a protective package design but a 
“shock treatment” one. Several antifungal additives will be placed instead MOFs, such as peptides, 
essential oils, nanoparticles, or quaternary ammonium. The Antifungal peptides3 and essential oils (used by 
AIMPLAS in pre vious projects related to active food packages) are natural source substances and they 
have diferrent  odour levels and efficiency againts bacteria and fungus. 
4. Design a modular smart package that fulfil all requirements of selected CH (cultural heritage) artefacts, 
such as easy change and recyclable adsorption/antimicrobial systems, exploiting spaces, hermetic seal, vacuum 
to remove all the oxygen after packing for anoxic packaging and competitive cost. 
5. Development of Chemi cal sensors based on the use of na notechnology, including electronic wireless 
devices, for degradation process monitoring, promoting the non -invasive techniques. Sensors integrated in the 
package will be designed to measure the following gases ( acetic acid, nitrogen oxides, moisture and ox ygen) 
all-in-one. There are few detectors/indicators commonly used for AA in conservation (electronic or chemical) 
and for oxygen too (fluorescent sensor). However the most used are A -D strips that measures a pH value and it 
requires to open the package an d direct contact with the movie or other artefact.  There are not in the market or 
related patents of integrated multisensors  based on nanotechnology for continious CH predictive maintenance.  
NEMOSINE proposes t he follow s olutions beyond the state of the a rt: i) O2 detection. ZnO nanorod 
photocurrent and porphyrine photoluminescence gas sensors integrates in optical fibers/waveguides for their 
miniaturization of the sensing devices, ii) NO detection. conductive polymers (polypyrrole and polyaniline) or 
combining ZnO nanostructures with conductive polymers or other metal oxides (such as CuO) for forming p -n 
junction. Resistivity or photocurrent measurements will provide good testing of NO and iii) AA detection. 
Similar conductive polymers than for NO detection and Optical absorbance More information in section 1.4.3 
In addition to the detection of gases planned in the project, the RFID chip will allow wireless communication 
of the integrated sensors results to the CH curators via a tailored software or control platform.  
6. To develop a model to link the measurement of AA and the other vapours to a degradation level . It will 
allow to predict the years before a severe degradation appears, in order to know when other conservation works 
are needed. Thus, the modular s mart package can be adapted and optimized with the required protective 
elements according to the degradative simulation results. In -line data measurements will allow to predict 
undesirable degradative processes and to program periodic maintenance actions.

1.3.4. Methodology. 
NEMOSINE is a 4 -year project. It is structured into 9 workpackages, as the PERT diagram below shows (figure 
1.3.d), which are linked to promote the cooperation of partners and to reach the target objective of NEMOSINE in 
the topic NMBP-35-2017. Each WP addresses a specific set of tasks needed to achieve sequentially the different 
goals and milestones set in the workplan  with the clear objective to reach and prepare 3 real prototypes or 
demonstrators where validate the protective and curative performance. WP1, WP2 and WP3 are  focused in the 
combination of different materials and polymeric structures to improve protection of CH artefacts, looking for 
sinergetic effects. WP1 will design the requirements and initial package  structure design; WP2 will develop MOF 
AA adsorbers and antifungal additives –where CNRS, IST and NPH will have a critical role -, while WP3 will 
integrate the active substances in high porosity environments: open cell foams and nanofibers (MODISPREM, 
AIMPLAS, NPH).  WP4 will wor k in the creation of a multisensor  array to monitor degradative gases 
(BIOSENSOR), that will be integrated in a wireless RFID and degradative simulation control system in the WP5 
(IRIS, IST). 
NEMOSINE will reach TRL6 in the WP6 developing and integrating all the systems in a whole smart and modular 
package, developing the defined prototypes and real demonstrators (PROM, IPC, AKUMPLAST), as well as full 
validation in different protective applications (relevant environments). WP7 wil l involve th e environmental and 
economic studies, while WP8 (communication, dissemination and exploitation) and WP9 (management) will act as 
transversal workpackages, supporting the rest ones. 
 
Figure 1.3.d. NEMOSINE partnership (main roles) and workplan structure and planned commercialization 
Moreover, some institutions have already expressed their interest in the NEMOSINE project results, signing a 
Letter of support (LoS), as it can be seen in Annex 1 at section s 4 -5.  These skateholders wi ll ensure tha t the 
development in NEMOSINE project are completely aligned with the current objetives and goals (see complete list 
of nine LoS in page 1).

The technologies, processes and prod ucts develop ed in NEMOSINE are gender -independent. All  NEMOSINE 
Partners have internal gender equality jobs creation and promotion policies. The consortium will foster the presence 
of women in the technical and management teams and decision board implemented to govern NEMOSINE project. 
The approach of NEMOSINE project is fully in line with D irective 2002/73/EC of the European Parliament and of 
the Council of 23 September 2002 on the implementation of the principle of equal treatment for men and women as 
regards access to employment, vocational tra ining and pro motion, and working conditions. A IMPLAS, as project 
coordinator, is currently developing an internal Gender Equality Plan. NEMOSINE project will be coordinated by 
Mrs. Giner. 
1.4. AMBITION 
1.4.1 State-of-the-Art and progress in acetic acid (AA) adsorbers. 
Photographs and cellulosic artefacts are sen sitive to pollutants and particularly VOCs. Certain dyes in color 
photographs are discolored not only by sulfur dioxide and oxidants such as ozone, nitrogen oxides but a lso by 
organic acids such as AA 6. The hydrolysis and oxidation of cellulose and cellulose esters/ethers is catalyzed by the 
AA (which is produced by the cellulose derivative heritage artefact itself) 7. There is an autocatalytic process that 
speeds up the movie film base degradation.  
Vinegar synd rome was asig ned in the beginning of 1980s as an effect of acetic acid emissions after cellulose 
triacetate degradation, reported innitially by Eastman Kodak Company in 19488, where, in a simplified manner, the 
true iniciator of degradation process is the water and accelerated by the continous production of AA.  
To capture this VOC, inorganic adsorbents such as cationic zeolites markedly slow down film deterioration 9, and 
thus allow to extend the longevity of a movie  film by a f actor of three to four. Howev er, this bene ficial effect is 
apparently related more to their ability to dry air than to the neutralization of acid gases 10. Furthermore, this effect 
is not pronounced enough for films that are in the process of det eriorating11a. Commercial systems such as 
MicroChamber®, Alphamat® and Artcare® 1b are composed of an assembly of paper layers, each with a different 
chemical composition, and the released AA is trapped by the zeolites (and active charcoal) dispersed through out 
the fibe rs. The efficiency is neverth eless limited  due to the diffusion process thr ough the fiber and the lower 
accessibility. 
Activated carbons (or charcoals) are another class of porous commercial adsorbents suitable to capture acetic acid. 
Activated Carbon Cloth (ACC) is an activated charc oal produced in a flexible textile form with a  large internal 
surface area (width slit-shaped micropores) with a proven adsorption efficiency. However, those ACC produce dust 
(charcoal powder) that is not compatible with the good conservation of many heritage artefacts.  
An alternative is to consider functionalized polymers, integrated into Static Intercept Films® and Corrosion 
Intercept® Polyethylene Films, originally intended for packaging and protecting electronic  equipment. These are 
made of polyethylen e combined wi th copper atoms that, as they oxi dize, intercept acetic acid. However, these 
systems suffer from diffusion and adsorption limitations hampering their efficiency.  
As stated above, the relative humidity in the air h as a significant (negative) i mpact on the performance of the 
adsorbent materials regarding acetic acid adsorption while the (ideal) storage under very low relative humidity is 
difficult to achieve. Thus, the development of adsorbents that can e ffectively capture acetic acid in the pre sence of 
relative humidity normally found at s torage in museums (40 -60%) is still a challenge and is a key point for the 
success of this project. For this, we will select and/or develop advanced porous materials tha t have the a bility to 
capture significant amounts of acetic acid in the presence of water vapour. 
Porous metal organic frameworks (MOFs) are a recent class of porous hybrid crystalline materials. Their chemical 
composition, structure and pore size/shape ca n be easily tailored in a much more preci se way than i n traditional 
adsorbents (zeolites, silicas, alumina, etc). They are constructed by the connection of inorganic nodes (clusters, 
chains, layers (see Figure 1.4.a)) with organic polycomplexing ligands, t hrough iono-covalent bonds. Their pore 
size can and be varied, from micro to mesopores, leading to several types of cages or channels (Figure 1). If at their 
early stages their practical use was hampered by their low moisture stability, the use of high val ence (III, IV) metal 
cations have recently led to seri es of robust, even hydrothermally  stable, MOFs.12 This is of interest to find MOF

7 Dupont et al., J. Cellulose degradation in an acetic acid environment, Studies in Conservation 45, 2000, 201-210.  
8 http://www.kodak.com/motion/support/technical_information/storage/vinegar_syndrome/default.htm

10 https://www.imagepermanenceinstitute.org/webfm_send/307

12 Devic et al., “High valence 3p and transition metal based MOFs”, Chem. Soc., Rev., 2014, 43(16):6097-115 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 14 of 110 
candidates highly suitable to adsorb amphiphilic VOC molecules such as acetic acid, even in the presence of water. 
One pa rticularly efficient strategy to further optimise the sorption properties of MOFs is to  consider the use of 
linkers bearing specific chemical surface groups that will allow a strong enhancement of their hydrophobic 
character13 and thus the selectivity of ad sorption within the final structure. Undi sclosed results (obtained by IST 
and CNRS) have indicated that this is a viable strategy, with some selected MOFs exhibiting an acetic acid capture 
efficiency that from far surpasses the ones of zeolites or carbons in the presence of moisture. Note that CN RS can 
produced up to the multi -hundred gram s cale all these MOFs using ambient pressure conditions. It has also been 
demonstrated, through BASF and more recently by SMEs such as MOFtech, MOFgen, MOFapps or PROM 
(among others), that MOFs can easily been pr oduced at the  industrial scale through differe nt synthesis methods 
(batch, thermomechanical, spray-drying, continuous flow…).14 
 
Figure 1.4.a. – Representation of a few topical moisture stable MOFs (in orange or blue, the inorganic node; in black, the 
aromatic organic spacer; in yellow, the accessible pore volume). Two dicarboxylate hydrophobic linkers on the right 
Beyond the state of the art,  NEMOSINE project aims to develop  a new line of AA adsorbers based on MOFs 
technology that will go beyond the state of the art li mitation outlined above will be a vailable to the conservation 
experts. To achieve this goal, two parallel and complementary strategies will be followed to maximize the changes 
of success. Two smart strategies to obtain MOFs highly selective for the capture of acetic acid are considered: 
i)  Hydrothermally stable amphiphilic or slightly hydrophobic MOFs such as the zinc imidazolate frameworks ZIFs 
(e.g. ZIF-8), the metal(III, IV) polycarboxylate UiO -66’s, MIL-53, MIL-88B, MIL-125, MIL-127 and MI L-140’s 
MOFs; note that one might tune their pore size through a modulation of the length of the organic spacer to optimize 
the confinement of acetic acid within the pores .  
ii)  Functionalized analogues of some of  the above-mentioned MOFs bearing fluorin ated or alkyl  groups on the 
linkers in order to further enhance the selectivity of acetic acid vs water. 
1.4.2 State-of-the-Art and progress in MOF polymer composites. 
In recent years, several MOF polymers composites have  been developed in a view of applications , including t he 
adsorption of organic compound s and gases. 15 Furthermore, many approaches have been successfully applied to 
immobilize other classic adsorbed in porous medias to produce filters with air purifying cap abilities.16 The 
following summary will be  focused on t hose more relevant for the envisi oned application of the MOF polymer 
composites for the NEMOSINE objectives. The MOF-foam composites are a good approach, avoiding much of the 
issues of the existing methods of application of adsorbents to the conservation of CH: 
• The MOF particles are immobilized in a polymeric matrix that avoids the dispersion of the particles throughout 
the CH artefacts. 
• Accessibility of the AA vapors to the MOF particles is high because  of the macroporous structure of the foams 
and fibrous substrates.  
• Enhanced interaction of AA compared to water due to the tailoring of the chemical surface properties of MOFs. 
• High adsorption capacity of the MOF composite foams and fibrous substrates due to the high surface areas that 
can be obtained with porous MOFs.

Three different approaches based on the proven methods from the literature will be used in NEMOSINE to obtain 
MOF polymer composites suitable for application in CH conservation packages: 1) to produce polyurethane foams 
with supported MOFs, 2) to produce electrospun fibers with MOFs and 3) to produce paper containing MOFs. The 
current state of the art for each approach is briefly reviewed below. 
Immobilization of powdered adsorbents in foams is usually achieved industrially by soaking foams with a slurry of 
adsorbents in water/ solvent in the presence of a binder (usually a polymer based one). This route gives several 
problems in the properties of the final material (adhesion problems, obstruction of the pores of the adsorbents, slow 
adsorption ki netics, significant decrease of a dsorption capacity) and requires a costly production process with 
several soaking/drying cycles to achieve a high loading of adsorbents. This even might require the surf ace 
functionalization of the MOF particles using polymers to enhance the colloidal stability of the MOFs particles into 
the solvent.  
 
Figure 1.4.b. Activated carbon / foam composite produced by a scaled-up process to obtain a macroporous media with 
adsorption capabilities.17 
Several researchers have already demonstrated the possibility of i ncluding MOF powders of small particle size in 
nonwoven fiber media, using electrospinning methods. 18 The MOF particles in the form of fine powders are 
suspended in a pol ymer solutio n that is then used to produc e fibbers ana logous to a common electrospinnin g 
process (Figure 1.4.a). The obtained fibers are very thin (Figure 1.4. b) and contain the MOF particles attached to 
them (Figure 1.4.c). Up to now the most promising p olymer/solution combination for such proc ess is 
polyacrylonitrile (PAN) in dimethylformamide (DMF). This polymer/solution is already widely used in industry to 
produce electrospinning fibers. Several MOFs have already been tested, like HKUST-1, MIL-100(Fe), ZIF-8, UiO-
66 and MIL -101(Cr). In the N EMOSINE project, the best MOFs developed for c apturing AA will be used in the 
production of the fibbers with MOFs. DMF is a convenient solvent for electrospinning and for MOFs stability. 
However, other more appropri ate solvents will be investigated for up -scaling since DMF is a toxic solvent that is 
more difficult to remove from the final processed material.

Finally, the MOF powders can be supported in cellu lose fiber m edia, using a paper like proc ess that was already 
successfully used to support other adsorbents.

(granulated of pellet forms), as discussed in the previous section, and then add  the particles into a foam re acting 
formulation, to obtain a one -shot foam with supported particles evenly distributed . This last strategy was already

1.4.3 State-of-the-Art and progress in antifungals for conservation and their encapsulation.  
Conservators are reluctant to add chemicals that might da mage or cont aminate a heritage object. Several works 
today are devoted to the removal of pesticides and chemical in museum artefacts. Developing a package that is both 
effective against microorganisms and harmless to humans, the environment, and photograph s is challen ging. 
Numerous chemicals have been tested for their fungistatic or fungicid e properties on heritage artefacts. These are 
generally alkylation agents (formaldehyde, ethylene oxide), organobromines (methyl bromide), quaternary 
ammonium (zinc fluorosilicate and Hyamine 1622), or phenol d erivatives (thymol, orthophenylphenol). The latter, 
which have long been recommended for graphic documents, are not very active on spores and might be harmful for 
photographs. Hyamine 1622, which is apparently usabl e on black a nd white images, is harmful t o certain col or 
chromogenic photographs, since  it reacts with cyan dye. Zinc fluorosilicate does not appear to be harmful to 
photographs, whether black and white or color. There is currently some interest in using e ssential oils extracted 
from plants such as rosemary, thyme, pine, eucalyptus, and citr onella. These natural essences contain phenol and 
terpene derivatives, which have antiseptic, bacteriostatic, and fungistatic properties. Those have to be tested for 
their effective ness against molds and harmfu lness for peo ple, environment and audio -visual artefacts. However, 
encapsulated essential oil has been proposed but it might be some issues with respect to health and interaction with 
objects. In the last years, the re are repor ts19 on the antifungal activit y of peptides  isolated from a broad range of 
medicinal plants that displayed antifungal activity toward several fungal species. They have less effectively than 
essential oils but are odor-less and lower effect to non-fungal items. 
Beyond the state of the a rt, NEMOSINE aims to develop new active packag e by encapsulating odour -free 
antifungals peptides a nd other antifungals to be integrated in high surface area devices (open cells foams and/or 
electrospinning nanofiber ) to maximiz e the action. The encapsulati on will allow  an accurate control of the 
substance release kinetics. Application of antifungals will have a curative  purpose by inhibiting the spread of 
moulds (fungistatic effect) on artefacts or eventually killed them (fungicide effect). 
 
 
1.4.4 State-of-the-Art and progress in sensor for acid vapours measurement using nanotechnology.  
Oxygen detection is normally performed by resistive gas 
sensors20. The main disadvantage of these sensors is their high 
operating temperat ure (300 -600 °C) due to transfer of heat 
activated ele ctrons between metal oxide surfac e and adsorbed 
oxygen. In order to reduce operating temperatures and enhance 
sensitivity, photocurrent -based sensors have been developed 21. 
Typical measurement scheme of photocurrent gas sensor is 
shown in Figur e 1.4.d. Elec tron-hole pairs were generated by  
UV excitation light source.  
Different metal oxides have been used in photocurrent gas 
sensors for oxygen detection. Typical sensor response of oxygen 
gas sensor, based on ZnO nanoribbons is shown in Figure 1.4.e.

on gas sensing based on surface photocurrent.

Surface Science,254, 2008, 2856–60. 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 17 of 110 
Photocurrent was measured when exposed to oxygen. The tests were 
performed in the range of O 2 pressure form 0.58 Torr to 15 T orr. 
Good repeatability and s tability of t he sensor were observed. Wang 
et al. 2016 reported on oxygen detection using TiO 2 nanorods. The 
developed resistive TiO 2 nanorod oxygen gas sensor showed 
sensitivity to 1-16 % of oxygen with limit of detection (LOD) 0.5%. 
Fluorescence of compl ex organic mo lecules such as porphyrins can 
be used for oxygen detection 22. The increase of oxygen partial 
pressure led to fluorescence quenching. The developed porphyrin -
based systems could simultaneously measure te mperature ch anges 
and oxygen pressure. Po rphyrin based  oxygen sensors have been 
shown g ood sensitivity to 0 -100% concentrations of oxygen in the 
temperature range of 25-65 °C.  
 
Figure 1.4.e. The surface photocurrent of ZnO 
nanoribbons exposed to three cycles of air–
vacuum with the illumination of 361 nm. 
In addition, good compatibility of  porphyrin-based oxygen sensors with commercial laser emitting diodes (LED) 
has been demonstrated.  NO sensing is traditionally performed by metal oxide sensors. Due to n anotechnology 
approaches, operating temperature was decreased to room temperature. However, response time and selectivity are 
still actual problems23. Current-voltage measurements of conductive polymers and metal oxide/conductive polymer 
nanostructures for NO gas detec tion have been reported.  Goo d sensitivity to NO was in the range of 5 -100 ppm 
with detection limit of 5 ppm has been achieved 24. In addition, UV treatment was used for stimulating of NO 
desorption and decreasing recovery time of the sensor. 
Detection of ac etic acid vapours is an actua l topic. Phot oluminescence of optically active  organogels and surface 
Plasmon resonance gold nanostructures, equipped with polypyrrole layer have been applied for acetic acid 
detection in air. The developed sensors showed good signal and stability to 10 -70 ppm acetic a cid at room 
temperature. Prospective approach for acetic acid detection has been demonstrated with optically active conducting 
polymers25. 
The developed conductive polymer layers are sensitive to the pH.  It was show n, that response of the condu ctive 
polymer sensor to HCl was much higher th an to acetic acid. However, modification of the selective layer could 
increase sensitivity to acetic acid. Particularly, it was demonstrated that hybrid inorganic/organi c nanostructures 
showed enhanced sensitiv ity of hybrid  nanostructures for VOC species. Therefore, combining hybrid 
nanostructures for electrical, optical and electro -optical detection of VOCs is a prospective research field. White 
source (torch of smartphone) or UV excitation source (LED) can be also used as the light source. Minimization and 
integration of three types of sensors into one unit will be foreseen. Additional testing of all sensing elements to 
water adsorption, cross sensitivity and selectivity will be performed. 
From the analysis of the recent ac hievements on room temperature de tection of O 2, NO and acetic acid (AA), 
NEMOSINE proposes the follow solutions beyond the state of the art: 
1. Oxygen detection can be performed by using a metal oxide a nd porphyrin nanostructures using photocurrent 
and photoluminescence spectroscopy as a technique to measure the sensor signal, respectively. 
2. NO sensing can be performed by metal oxide and metal oxide/conductive polymer using photocurrent 
technique. 
3. Acetic acid sensing can be performed by conductive polymers using optical spectroscopy. 
4. The detection system can be integrated  on one chip and equipped with UV LED as excitation source 
directly in the modular package design.  
1.4.5 State-of-the-Art and progre ss in mathem atical models to predict degr adation in CH  cellulose based 
artefacts. 
Literature concerning modelling experimental data of the relationship between cellulose derivatives’ degradation 
stages (cellulose acetate (CA) and cellulose nitrate (CN) and  any of their physical or chemical characteristic in CH 
 
 
22 X. Zhou, Platinum (II) porphyrin -containing thermoresponsive poly(N -isopropylacrylamide) copolymer as fluorescence dual oxygen and

Page 18 of 110 
artefacts is very scarce. The f irst reference deals with chemometrics 26a reports near infrared (NIR) to correlate the 
mechanical behaviour of papers used in paints and photography with their degradatio n condition. Afterwards only 
Strlič’s res earch group 13b described some studies on NIR s pectral data’s multivariate analysis app lied to CA 
negative films and photographic papers. NIR is a very fast in situ, non -destructive technique, easily enabling 
material’s condition assessment, but it is expensive and difficult to integrate in a package. 
IST and NOVA partners27 have the expertise of characterising and modelling the results of more than three hundred 
CA and CN black & white film negatives naturally aged, with different preservation conditions, formats and brands 
belonging to six different ph otographic and movie collections hosted by national archives. These complete set of 
characterisation results (considered to be representative of collections found in a common archive) will be available 
to this project and will be used as reference samples in order to test different modelling procedures prior to test data 
obtained from the sensors developed under this project’s framework.  
The application of hybrid modelli ng to CH inv olving the application of curve resolution methods to extract 
degradation chemically-related data from spectra of c ellulose derivatives was not attempted yet. This methodology 
proved to be very promising as documented in other CH items 28. If tested on data available can provide additional 
accurate insight about degradation levels on different temporal scales. Hybrid mod els will then be simulated 
resourcing to open platforms for simulation encompassing predictable environmental conditions to estim ate the 
degree of degradation expected under different storage conditions. 
In this prop osal modelling will be applied to data a cquired by the developed gas sensors located inside designed 
barrier film packages for cellulose derivatives artefacts. These sensors will monitor released degradation gases such 
as acids, nitrogen oxides and CO 2. Th ese models are expected to suggest recom mendations for predictive 
conservation (e.g. cold, temperature, adsorbents, antifungal agents).  
Beyond the state of the art,  NEMOSINE aims t o develop multi -scale models to correlate sensors’ signals  
integrated in the package with degradation level of any type of cellulose derivatives CH artefacts. The correlation 
between sensor signals and degradation stage will be mainly achieved using multi-scale chemometric tools . 
Hybrid models, the combination of predictive chemo metric methods (e.g., partial least squa res, feedforward neural 
networks) and known chemical degradation mechanisms, are the key for an accurate estimation of the evolut ion of 
degradation over time and will be tested with the available data. 
1.4.6 State-of-the-Art and progress in injection moulding barrier module packages. 
The presence of oxygen accelerates the degradation of old cellulose derivative items. Well known non -
conventional injection moulding techniques that include the combination of two or more mater ials with different 
chemical structure a s over moulding, co -injection (or sandwich injection) and also IML (in mould labelling) can 
help to reduce the entry of oxygen on the package or reduce the vacuum required to remove the initial oxygen 
inside of the package.  
Different polymeric materials a re suitable as high oxygen and moisture barriers 29, taking into account the injected 
thicknes of package layers, and the effective ness of materials. Some potential cand idates for NEMOSINE project 
are: 
Water barrier pr operties: polypropylene (PP), Polyethyle ne (PE); Oxygen barrier properties : PET (polyethylene 
terephtalate), PA (polyamide) or EVOH (Ethylene Vynil Alcohol) , Aluminium foils or SiOx coatings (If in-mould 
labeling technology is employed). 
These materials give together good chemical response with moderated price, and easy processing behaviour. But, 
the most important aspect is the possibility to integrate in a easy way ever y modular technology able to protect the 
CH artefacts. 
Injection moulding is a well kno w and mature process that is used in sev eral industrial sectors (packaging, 
automotive, electric electronic, ,,,) to produce from hundreds to millions of parts at low co st and short  time (less 
than half a minute per part in average). The injection moulding  allows the fabrication of a broad range  of 3D parts 
with a free design and the posibilities to integrate other materials or parts, t oothbrushes or screwdrivers are 
examples of multi-component parts at low cost.  This technology will permit to combine diffe rent materials in the 
same parts by usin g co -injection or overmoulding, or to incorporate a high barrier films (contaings inorganic 
coatings or aluminium foils) by in-mould labeling.

Furthermore, injection moulding allows to build different sizes or shapes  parts just by modify some parts of the 
metallic mould. For example, it is easy to perform different holes or specific places in the package to integrate 
the sensors or the vacuum system, or internal ribs to easily integrate the foams or nanofibers. Beyond the state 
of the art, NEMOSINE aims to develop the best integration technologies in order to design the best package for 
full protecting of the original audio -visual CH artefacts. Oxygen and moisture barrier, vacuum and suitable 
design for easy mounting a nd dismounting of package elements (sens ors, adsorbers, communications, etc) will 
be proposed. Finally, the objective is to achieve a realistic processing terms of future scale-up. 
1.4.7 Main competitors.  
Some commercial products are available in the mar ket, such as PIQLBox© 30. This solution ad vocate for the 
substitution of original acetate substrate, making a copy of the audiovisual content in a new PET durable film 
substrate, combined with a rigid package of a non -degradable polymer. This solution do not  protect the original 
audiovisual material, but, replacing it by a more resistant support device. Other solutions, such as MicroChamber©, 
Artsorb tissue©, Alphamat®, and Artcare®6b are composed of an assembly of paper layers, each with a different 
chemical composition.  
The release of AA are detected by using colored paper indicator (AD-strip)  and trapped by the active charcoal and 
zeolites that are  dispersed through th e fibers. Th e efficiency is limited due to the diffusion process through the 
fiber and the lower accessibility, as well as huge limitations on durability, chemical, mechanical and environmental 
resistance. 
Sensorized commercial packages, such as DANCAN CINEMA SERVICES, include indicator paper strips for only 
acetic acid detection with very l ow sensitivity, far from the complete so lution proposed by NEMOSINE based on 
multisensoric nanosensors for different gases (O 2, AA, NO) and a control software platform t o simulate 
degradation processes and then predict accurate protective treatments.  
NEMOSINE will offer three types of packages  (BASIC PREVENTIVE, PREMIUM PREVENTIVE and 
CURATIVE) as an innovative solution for the conservation of the ORIGINAL audiovisual co ntent. Proje ct 
model business is based on a double objective:  
a) On the on hand, NEMOSINE  innovative packaging will contribute to  decrease on 4.6 M€/y related to 
economic damages due to work loses that currently take place every year (assuming that NEMOSINE will 
prevent 2.25% of the loses during the first three years of their commercialization). 
b) At the same time, NEMOSINE will open a new conservation market to be exploitaed through a joint venture 
and licenses outside Europe, estimated in a turnover of  35 M€/y (5 years after the project ends).

developed mathematical model, which will estimate the long -term optimal pre dictive 
maintenance plan for each monitored CH artifact. The real time data from RFID  will feed the 
predictive model s to be used  in the decision support platform for the conservers and make a 
significant step in the knowledge management regarding CH maintenance. 
The use of sensors, which data will be made publically available and be centralised remotely in a 
cloud platform (to feed the proprietary decision support systems used by the CH conservers) will 
contribute to build the IoT (Internet of Things) in th e community of audio -visual archives and 
libraries.

quantified socio -
economic gains from the 
proposed solutions. 
The proposed solution is economically driven and optimized for efficient preservation and long 
term conservation of fragile  and precious material for future generations. This means better 
financial investments to protect expensive artefact s, and the photographs and films that contain a 
significant part of our common memories and cultural legacy for the future. There are audio -
visual items without value that will be used as samples for the tests, as a baseline, to validate the 
improvements of NEMOSINE solution.   
There is a clear need for inexpensive, reliable and user friendly tools in the CH audio -visual 
sector. The products w ill be suitable for any collection containing cellulose derivative artefacts, 
without limitation to 20th century obj ects. Thus, the market potential is large. By improving 
protection of 20th century heritage through passive enclosures and sensors, NEMOSINE  
contributes to develop the socio -economic gains in the CH sector by ensuring long term access, 
to a larger communit y at a lower  cost. NEMOSINE generates a new sector for conservation 
products.

2.1.1 Enhancing innovation capacity and integration of new knowledge. 
Being a RIA project up to TRL 6, the NEMOSINE process value chain has been devised as an industry -driven. 
Every partner has understood the whole applied research and technolo gy developme nt cycle ensuring the 
cooperation of entities close to market, end -users and the requirements set by them. No independent tasks are 
possible, going ahead as a “unique company” to pre -marketable CO2 capture product. The project offers all 
partners involved new possibilities to improve their innovation capacities and new knowledge in business, 
technological, social, environmental or some combination of them in a real collaboration to achieve so. 
Article 3.3 of the Lisbon treaty states that the Uni on “shall respect its rich cultural and linguistic diversity, and 
shall ensure that Europe's cultural heritage is safeguarded and enhanced .” There is an ambition at European 
level to make Europe a laboratory for “heritage -based innovation”31. This backdrop is highlight favourable for the 
introduction of cost effective and high performance technologies, such as NEMOSINE, that can assist Europe i n 
realising its ambitions and in preserving our 20th century audio-visual cultural heritage32.  
NEMOSINE´s ultimate g oal has an i ntrinsic utility since the conservation of the CH at long term will result in

who come from numerous different academic fields . Not only f rom the traditional ‘heritage’ disciplines of 
conservation/restoration with an important role, but including other technical fields, such as IT, chemistry, safety.

products will satisfy the demanding requirements of their different types of end-users/clients (both the conventional 
citizens and the expert SSH organizations).  Currently, as an example, a ‘ventilating circular box’ (39cm diameter;

Figure 2.1.b. Estimated models package costs for a rectangular theoretical shape of 40x40 cm and 300g of weight. 
Protective package for CH audio-visuals. One of the notorious gaps in the field of audio -visual preservation is an 
estimation of the total amount of materials stored in collections worldwide based on counts or at least serious 
estimations. There are several surveys attempting to finding out for example how many film works are held in EU 
film archives:  EU projects Presto 33a and TAPE 2b, ACE survey 34 or OEAW survey 35. However, to calculate 
NEMOSINE economic impact and the business forecast , the most recent PricewaterhouseCoopers (PWC) study 
(2015) has been used36.  
Audio-visual collections can be grouped as follows: 1) (partly) autonomous audio -visual research archives; 
memory institutions, such as libraries, archives and museums; departments of research or cultural institutions, local 
museums, oral history societies, etc.., 2)  materials privately owned by the researchers, collectors or  audio -visual 
buff that created audio and video documents for their research purposes and  3) private owne rs that keep own old  
family photographs (and/or their negatives), movies or audio. 
The products to be designed within the project are highly interesting for collections of cinematographic materials 
(film archives), as well as audio archives holding historical materials on basis of cellulose derives. Specifically, the 
estimation of such holdings within EU major professional film archives is around 5 Million film items37 or 18 
Mio of film reels (cans) on cellulose acetate.  This value must be multiply by 3 to c alculate all the items made by 
cellulose derivates and that belong to the European Heritage or families or towns memories (~50 Millions). 
As another example of uncertainty, the number of materials based on acetate derivative held within collections 
outside FIAF (Fédération In ternationale des Archives du Film),  the archival community or within private 
collections is unknown, but can be estimated as very high,  as materials on cellulose derivative have been 
produced until ca. mid of 1970’s (audio), respectively until recently (cinematographic materials). Additionally there 
is a huge number of microfilms held in libraries , which were produced on cellulose derivative, now partly 
suffering from vinegar syndrome or other negative effects of material decomposition38, such as migration or loss of

preservative package. To storage these items required a place with low temperature and controlled humidity. It is 
expensive for large museums and archives and difficult to manage and expensive for individual families with a few 
number of cellulose artefacts.

Curative package for CH audio-visuals. According the PWC study36,  5% film prints or negatives (items) are in 
a critical stage or showing signs of vinegar syndrome (unusable due to chemical decomposition processes) or are 
under other types of fungus attach. From the economic impact and based on previous mentioned PWC stu dy the 
damage assessed at EU level is theoretically ca. 23 M€ per year ( 5% of the total works), only for EU film 
archives. NEMOSINE project aims to reduce those losses in 15%, which will potentially reduce economic damage 
by 3.5M€ in Europe annually. 
 This is the result of considering that manufacturing a photochemical substitute costs between 4.000 € (for a short 
film) & 10.000 € (and more) for a feature-length film. These numbers can easily triple when protecting also photos, 
or other media supports. In fact, the estimation does not even include television archives, private collectors and the 
home movie/amateur film market, and the loses costs do not take into account the costs if staff time at CH 
institutions dedicated to detecting and separating film elements in decomposition state. 
NEMOSINE are enablers for innovation in the conservation of all those types of products mentioned 
(films, photos, audios, etc), and will face the existing negative decomposition effects throughout innovative 
curative packaging solution so many different and varied target end -users in Europe and internationally 
(FIAF, private collections and others). The project will reduce those economic loses, by opening a new type of 
conservation market (a new niche market).  
The expected impact of the curative package are quantified in table 2.1.d based on an expected market share of the 
20% of the European professional market of items with some conservation problems in 2028.  The expected prices 
of the curative package will be significant lower to  current storage solutions based on curative actions directly to 
the damaged artefacts. Furthermore controlled release antifungals is a safe curative method for the conservation 
people and less aggressive regeneration for the artefacts.

In summary, the project will generate five-six years after project finish a turnover of more tha n 30.3M€/year, more 
than 150 employee/year (based on the estimation of 1 job/200 k€ of turnover) and near to 4.5 M€/year of net profit 
(before taxes). High economic impact will be achieved through strengthening the competitiveness of the Industrial 
& End-user Partners in the target market sectors and related ones  (adsorbents-(activated carbons and zeolites), 
gases barrier films, sensors for air control, etc.)  by: 1) promoting the use of NEMOSINE  materials, components 
and systems  in the CH visual and audio m emories new packaging formats, while keeping costs competitive, 2) 
strengthening and differentiating the EU Industry, 3) increasing workers’ skills.  
Move on to the end -user innovation impacts, in our post -industrial economies, the culture and creative sec tors are 
increasingly becoming motors of the economy and indeed of employment. EU -wide data in particular are lacking, 
but sectorial and country -based studies indicate that the heritage sector makes a significant economic 
contribution41, i.e., it is estimat ed that around 20% of tourist trips worldwide incorporate some form of cultural, 
heritage or historical activity. As a global goal of the project, NEMOSINE aims to open up the market to promote 
the usage of this new storage solution in the visual imaging s ector, offering a solution that should be economically 
driven and, at the same time, strong and well -built for long durability, contributing to decrease the current 
economic loses due to audiovisual works which end up unusable every year. 
NEMOSINE’s market analysis based on Porter's five forces tool42 is presented in the following pages:  
Production rate: The production rate highly depends on the acceptance of the product. Archives have to be very 
conservative in the strategy and are generally underfunded an d heavily suffering from lack of staff. Therefore it is 
difficult to enter the market, especially if the product is not convincingly verified and does not represent a real 
proven innovation, which is what NEMOSINE will overcome through the fabrication and fully validation of 3 
DEMO-packages and generated data supporting the product benefits.  
Currently, one of the main reasons limiting the conservation/preservation capabilities is the manual character that 
reduce their implementation and increase costs (e.g . changing a box for a film reel needs manual handling, and 
therefore is time consuming and costly). The same is the case for controlling the climate within boxes etc.  
Some large archives have recently invested huge amounts of funds in the installation of  new storage vaults and 
climate control (e.g. cold storage). Those might have a big problem in argumentation in relation to their funders to 
request further funds for storage optimisation, however, both NEMOSINE’s package solutions are complementary 
to cold storage, due to they can used for new acquisitions or to increase the temperature of storage (energy & cost 
savings). There is still a huge amount of archives and private collections which have no access to cold storage.  
The actual tendency within the a rchival community is related to digitisation and digital restoration of audio/film 
content, which is still very complex, costly and time consuming. As this is on one hand a disadvantage, because 
related activities are proceeding very slowly, this is on the other hand a big chance for new fully proven innovative 
packaging solutions: It is conclusive, that valuable materials that have just been restored and digitised in a time 
consuming and costly procedure should be kept under most protective conditions to s ecure their future long time 
storage. This is the chance to place a highest quality product in the market.  
Therefore, the market will introduce new solutions very slow but steadily, if they are working effectively, 
according to the market acceptance of th e new product. Probably on the first couple of years it will be limited to 
few thousand pieces/year. Especially the conclusive positive verification of such innovative packaging solutions in 
cooperation with well -respected laboratories and high ranking tes t clients can convince future customers, as 
positive recommendations are ultimately valuable within this sensitive market.  
Cost: If the package is sold to replace only the conventional boxes for audio -visual artefacts, we are not 
competitive. However, NEMOSINE must be sold on long time storage of extremely valuable and unique materials. 
In this case costs could be several times higher than conventional boxes, if designed with highly innovative 
conservative and proven long time protective properties.   
Future challenge in the sector:  The complexity of the material is the most challenging factor to evaluate their 
future degradation under different storage conditions. Although a lot of research has been already conducted 
 
 
41 Communication of the Commission to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee & the 
Committee of the Regions. Towards an integrated approach to cultural heritage for Europe. Brussels, 22.7.2014. COM(2014) 477 final 
42 It is a framework for analysing the level of competition within an industry and business strategy development //en.wikipedia. org/wiki/ 
Porter%27s_five_forces_analysis. 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 26 of 110 
concerning cellulose derivative and rel ated deterioration mechanisms in audio -visual media, especially in 
cinematographic film materials, the microclimate in storage containers is still a relevant topic. Long -time effects 
are very difficult to predict and to measure in a comparative manner. Exi sting data are not public accessible, 
predictive maintenance simulation tools is very useful in these cases. 
Additionally, preservation is very important in our society, however less and less money is available through 
institutions and individuals to inves t on it. The funding situation for heritage institutions such as museums, 
archives, public and private collections, libraries etc. is critical and money is used for copying and digitisation. 
While digitisation is still very expensive and time consuming, th is might change within the next few years due to 
rise of the technology and competitors. Many institutions (e.g. broadcasters) will then even destroy materials of less 
high value (e.g. copies, various stages of intermediate materials) during the process of  copying and digitisation and 
therefore the need of packaging solutions will shrink. However, still it will be of high relevance the cellulose 
supports despite the digitisation, as those cellulose conserve information/contents that are not transferred in 
most cases, and that it will be necessary to repeat in the future. For example, in the case of films, still there will 
be an unavoidable long-term need to preserve millions of film cans.  
There is a tendency where potential competitors can sell low quality products and enter into the market. In a poorly 
educated society the risk is that many people will move their interest away from trusty solutions to poorly and 
cheap products. Therefore, the education will become an essential key selling vehicle.  
Existing Competition, Materials Suppliers& Potential New Entrants: The actual competitors are: 
a)  storage and acidity monitoring solutions developed by the former market leader and therefore most trusted 
company in motion picture film production, Eastman Kodak : mole cular sieves /zeolith www.kodak.com/ 
motion/support/people_and_planet/product_use/molecular_sieve/default.htm 
b) Highly trusted institution: Image Permanence Institute www.imagepermanenceinstitute.org/ 
c) Storage solutions based on these research activities:  http://dancan.dk/-   they manufacture  boxes and acid 
acetic detectors (24 hour test and sensors); www.stilcasing.com/ 
d) Other mentioned competitors of non -functional and simple packages designed for this sector: University 
Products, Light Impression, Container Store, Ryderbox, DyF,etc. 
e) Example of a potential new entrant: It is being introduced on the marke t the use of the photochemical film of 
35mm (Piql company) as support for the long -term data conservation. Technology launched in 2014 as a result 
of a research project, now commercialized in 17 countries, offering Digital Preservation services 43. Despite its 
progressive implementation, the proposed solution does not convince the film archives, not due to the film 
support, but because it is a new technology without any guarantee on its durability at long -term. It could be 
used as a complementary target for the NEMOSINE development. 
f) Other solutions in cellulose paper -sheet supports such as MicroChamber©, Artsorb tissue©, Alphamat®, and 
Artcare®6b with zeolites as acetic acid adsorbers but poor mechanic and long-time resistance. 
In summary, there are not in the market any similar solution for this sector and the possibilities to offer tailor-made 
and modular solutions open a broad range of different customers with different needs of conservation and economic 
capabilities. 
Main customers (end -users): content prov iders, film archives, museums, galleries, photographic archives, 
multimedia repositories, visual imaging institutions, etc. Note that within the consortium there are already two film 
archives (DFI & CulturArts), one audio archive (OEAW) and one photographi c entity (ALINARI), in addition to 
CXD, as Industrial provider of high quality conservation products to all of those

achievement of the expected benefits. Considering the facts and not m ere speculations, NEMOSINE will carefully 
monitor the design, implementation and managing of all components through the innovation manager and IPREB.

expected impact is described below, which will result in a strengthening competitiveness, internationalization and 
increased productivity through access to the potential market and an increased high added value product portfolio 
of NEMOSINE’s partners.

• MOFs capable of removing effectively acetic acid and other carbonyl based VOCs and MOF/foam 
composites maintaining the adsorbent properties of single MOFs  (IST, CNRS, PROM, AIMPLAS, 
MODISPREM). The business model proposed by these partners would be to p atent to protect the MOF and MOF 
foam applications, and use the validations in NEMOSINE. PROM will produce the MOF at industrial scale and 
MOISPREM will be in charge OF MOF/Foams. To improve the impact (far markets or for application to removal 
of VOCs in other CH environments), both companies aim to licence and  production of MOF and MOF/foam 
composites to external companies in agreement with IST, CNRS and AIMPLAS. 
• Nanofibre carriers of MOFs and antifungals (NPH & partially CNRS). NPH will develop during the project 
non-functionalised nanofibre carrier produced on a scale used for NPH’s research activities. Moreover, altogether 
with CNRS, antifungals will also be investigated. The validated  functionalised nanofibre carrier of MOFs, 
antifugals will be ready for commercial offering – with evaluation of scale-up requirements, after the project´s end. 
NPH aims to expand their material portfolio by processing of new innovative polymers. They will also generate 
new IP created in collaboration with other partners, which will be protected by means of Trade secret (in the case 
of the formulations of input materials and protocols concerning their processing into nanofiber structures), and 
patent, in collaboration with other partners, if applicable. The exploitation rou tes include the possibility of a) 
Contract R&D for manufacturers interested in using the nano -carrier system (feasibility studies, full development 
studies), b) Contract manufacturing (i.e. series for experimental validation); c) Licensing of the patent to  parties 
interested in integrating an antifungal/antimicrobial nano-carrier system with extended controlled release or placing 
their biaoctive candidated into such carrier. 
• New Air quality control, NO and oxygen sensors (BIOSENSOR, IRIS). BIOSENSOR with the support of 
IRIS (specialist in sensors and monitoring) for the airless integration of the sensor plans to develop a new series of 
sensor concept, with new functionalities. BIOSENSOR (owner of technology) and collaborators will form the 
management structure of the IPR based on the patentability of new developments. Ownership of IP rights will be 
jointly owned by the partners of the project and will be proportionally distributed among the partners according to 
the contribution of research and technological development. IRIS exploitation interest is in RFID based solution for 
CH package including the wireless communication system and control platform . IRIS´s exploitation route is direct 
sales and licensing. Customers would respectively be the mu seums /other archive conservers and the producers of 
equipment for this segment. Possibilities of licensing for outside markets or other detection applications, 
• Degradation software -Simulation models (NOVA/IST). The generated data and the basic models to develop 
at laboratory level for some unfinished packaging formats (software & hardware) are not under IPR protection and 
they will be available free or incorporated in platforms open source. Specifically, for IST and NOVA there will not 
have IPR related with software. IRIS will keep confidential the final versions and incorporate as an element in the 
predictive maintenance tools for the PREMIUM PREDICTIVE package. Future commercial agreements between 
IRIS and IST and NOVA will be possible for further versions with new or improved functionalities. 
• Innovative package for CH audio -visuals (IPC, AIMPLAS and AKUMPLAST): AIMPLAS & IPC will 
own the complex barrier films architectures and overmoulding process to produce the high -barrier packaging. 
Smart packaging design including easy mounting and dismounting of sensors and RFID system will be provide by 
the three partners, i.e., AKUMPLAST will contribute to the manufacturing of injection mould and injection 
moulding of the new packages development, but, the fu ll design adap ted to  the CH customers, simulation and 
initial prototypes will be shared between IPC and AIMPLAS.

2.1.4 Environmental and Cultural Heritage relevant impacts. 
Environmental impact:  will b e reduc ed because new packages will be marketed using environmentally friendly 
technical solutions compared to the current climatic chambers (controlled temperature and humidity) for the case of 
PREMIUM Preventive & Conservative formats (fo r the SSH organi zations). For example, NEMOSINE package s 
offer less energy consumption, less GHG emissions and less chemicals derivated from refrigeration process. 
The calculations are based on a conservative rough estimation focused only on film archives (although photography 
and other audio -visual archives can also use this conservation methodology, so the impact will be higher). If it is 
assumed that half of the largest film archives (approximately 81) use the climatic conservation option, with an 
energy use each one of 38.400 Kwh/y and a cost of 18,.000 €/y. 
The use of NEMOSINE packages will directly result in annual energy savings of around 9.3 Mkwh and 4.4 M€ for 
the film archive industry at worldwide level. This also results in a reduction of GHG emissions of 1,540 tonnes 
CO2 eq. 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 29 of 110 
Moreover, NEMOSINE  products also protect people from breathing acidic gases or manipulate objects acid 
impregnated; the new sensors to be developed will guarantee concentrations non dangerous for health (i.e acetic 
acid concentration: below 10 ppm; NO concentration: below 2 5 ppm.), and fibres are fully recyclable, so there is 
also a positive impact on the raw materials use (promoting the recycled materials versus the virgin ones).  
Employment impact: Europe's cultural heritage is also a precious asset in economic terms 44, wit h over 20,000 
museums45 employing over 100,000 people and contributing over €3 billion in revenue to the economy.  Reduction 
of conservation costs associated to handling, energy consumption, facilities maintenance, etc. will be devoted to 
widen the employme nt of highly skilled technicians in charge of the CH studies. As an example, based on the 
information received from NEMOSINE SSH partners, more than 10% of their annual budget is allocated to these 
functioning costs, that could be destined to contact new personnel or grant students to improve the CH knowledge. 
NEMOSINE aims at a contributing significantly in the number of jobs that CH sector will create in the coming 
years. We expect at least  150 qualified jobs directly  related to the manufacturing and sale  of new smart 
packaging products five years after the end of the project (when TRL8 will be achieved), based on a very 
conservative European market share. Additionally, it is estimated a creation of indirect 500 highly qualified jobs 
in the SSH organizations based on the above detailed data.  
In order to remain competitive and maintain jobs in the light of digitalization challenges and rising low quality 
markets in the developing world, the European CH conservation industry sector needs to innovate and furt her 
diversify. In the addressed CH archives, new skilled personnel will be needed to replace the packages, to control 
the IT sensors and improve the current simulation tools.  
2.1.5 Policy framework 
NEMOSINE scope, covering several types within the audiovisual w orks (audio, films, images, etc.), is in line with 
several Commission Recommendations and Communications launched in the last decade and even previously, with 
the aim of having a common vision for CH, starting for example from the Recommendation for the Sa feguarding 
and Preservation of Moving Images (1980) , through EU Recommendation 2005/865/CE of 16 November 2005 and 
Communciation on State of aid for films and other audiovisual works (14 November 2013), till Council conclusions 
on European Audiovisual Policy in the Digital Era (2014/C 433/02).  
Specifically, NEMOSINE will be complemetnary to Joint Programming Iniative on Cultural Heritage and 
Global Change: A new Challenge for Europe (JPICH ), which covers CH in a widen view (tangible & 
intangible), so NEMOSINE will be included in its the Strategic Research Agenda (SRA) on Cultural Heritage, i.e. 
4th pillar-‘Safeguarding our cultural heritage sources’ and its vision document 46, contributing to its general goals, 
encouraging and providing new solutions, in this case in ORIGINALS audiovisual conservation. 
Furthermore, NEMOSINE will develop a parallel solution (a new conservative cost competitive technology and 
best practices) to the current digitisation trend, focused on the ORIGINAL works. In that way, NEMOSINE will be 
complementary to initiatives as the following EU projects: 1. EFG -European Film Gateway; 2.FORWARD-Rights 
Resgistry for Audiovisual and Orphan Works , where precisacely DFI was  partner; and 3 .Filmarchives Online, to 
organizations such as PrestoCentre; as well as other still ongoing EU projects, with wider scope (under the JPICH), 
such as JHEP-2 (‘Support to the implementation of the Strategic Research Agenda (SRA) of the Joint Programming 
Initiative on Cultural Heritage and Global Change (JPI CH) ) and HERITAGE PLUS Era-net. As the CH is funded 
apart from NMBP and Societal Challenge 5,under Societal Challenge 6 ‘Inclusive, innovative and reflective 
societies’, some other EC potential projects with synergies have been found, with which NEMOSINE will int eract 
through its project life and beyond47.   
More generally, NEMOSINE  fully aligns and supports the EU Innovation Policy for Competitiveness and 
Growth and the EU 2020 strategy , as the outcome of NEMOSINE will have significant impact from the citizens 
as a whole (individual or private collections), through local museums and private relevant collections to major 
museums, as well as all the manufacturers involved in those smart packaging (i.e. industrial producers of MOFs 
adsorbers, active foams and nanofibe rs, encapsulated antifungals, sensors, degradation software, package  and 
functionalities integration) and all industrial other application sectors with the potential of using those new 
separated products. This will contribute to the EU Strategy for Key Ena bling technologies 48 by advancing the 
knowledge in latest technologies to provide advanced materials. High economic impact will be achieved through 
increasing the competitive advantage of EU Industry by promoting the use of NEMOSINE  smart packaging

the digitisation.
