2.2 MEASURES TO MAXIMISE IMPACT. 
Communication, dissemination and demonstration activities are critical for the successful exploitation of 
NEMOSINE research and innovation findings and accordingly a whole WP will be dedicated to these actions 
(WP8). Communication, dissemination and exploitation are linked activities and must be undertaken in a 
coordinated way, thus exploiting synergies and avoiding overlap between them; in NEMOSINE they will be 
coordinated by a Dissemination and Exploitation Board  (IPREB, see section 3.2.). Activities and their impacts 
will be continuously monitored during the projec t and the resulting actions reported in the interim & final Plan 
for Exploitation and Dissemination of the Results (PEDR), due in months 12, 30 & 48. 
NEMOSINE will implement a range of activities to ensure the optimal visibility of the project and its resu lts, 
increasing the likelihood of market uptake of the knowledge it produces, and ensuring a smooth handling of the 
individual intellectual property rights of the involved partners to pave the way to knowledge transfer and 
exploitation. Table 2.2.a summari zes the focus of activities and how the dissemination and exploitation plan fit 
together to produce the overall PEDR.

Communication activities will use a range of communication channels to spread new knowledge and results 
generated by the project. They aim at reaching the dissemination objectives and reinforcing the plausibility of the 
exploitation plan. In order to carry out the project outreach in a comprehensive way, a detailed communication plan 
will be implemented at the beginning of the project (month 6). It will aim to maximize the impact and visibility of 
the project among all relevant stakeholders at European level. 
The clear categorisation of target groups  allows dedicated and targeted dissemination actions to be undertaken 
through specific communication channels and using targeted messaging. 
Our communication plan encompasses a comprehensive series of actions (Table 2. 2.b) to broadcast the non -
confidential results that are generated during the project to as wide and relevant an audience as possible  in 
order to heighten awareness about the results, to contribute to knowledge building in Europe, and to ensure that as 
many actors and citizens as possible have access to these results.

2.2.2 Dissemination 
The main communication activities are focused on the dissemination of technical information to industry . The 
goal is to disseminate NEMOSINE objectives and results among the interested industry sectors, demonstrating the 
added value, innovation and new technologies developed within the project. Due to the relevance of this target 
audience, the position of the project consortium within the industry is very important. 
The goal of our communication activities will be to disseminate technical information both to the industry and the 
scientific community. Project results will be disseminated through participation in international conferences and 
trade fairs, and through publications in peer reviewed scientific journals and trade publications in the area of 
biochemistry, polymer processing, bioplastics, etc. Publication in Scientific Conferences  related to the 
NEMOSINE R&D areas will be also issued. Table 2.2.c details the number of publications and the journals where 
the consortium plans to contribute. The project will disseminate the results to business stakeholders to make them 
aware of the expected impact of the project and promote the exploitation  of its results. Presentations shall be made 
by the partners at business seminars and trade fairs. Additionally, each of the partners will disseminate 
NEMOSINE results in the fairs and exhibition they participate.

Data Management Plan. NEMOSINE project is fully aware of the open access to scientific publications as stated 
in art. 29.3. of the H2020 Grant Agreement. Open Access will be provided to peer -reviewed papers published by 
NEMOSINE’s Partners as table 2.2.c indicates, either in an open access journal repository (“green” model) or for 
instance using the OpenAire orphan repository. Depending on the results published, the selection of the best suited 
and higher impact repositories will be made on a case by case basis in cooperation with OpenAIR provided that 
the IPREB does not identify issues  conflicting with the industrial exploitation of project developments. Technical 
press platforms, generic or specific, will be continuously used, as well as the own partners communication 
channels. According to the H2020 guidelines, a Data Management Plan (DMP) will be created by using the FAIR 
EC system. A deliverable (first version) will be provided in month 6, and updated subsequently. Following the call 
recommendations, part of the modelling data (software data) will be shared in this DMP, based on the criteria of 
providing access only to those developed models developed at lab level, in intermediate packaging versions not 
100% finished).  
Networking: In addition to the direct commercial contacts of NEMOSINE industrial partners, wider dissemination 
would be achieved through using the partner memberships of trade associations related to the aims of the project. 
Working with trade associations the Consortium would increase the potential for exploitation of project results and 
additionally create a mutual op portunity with the associations to promote the conservators, within the relevant 
industrial sectors. Moreover, the know -how transfer of NEMOSINE to the European industry could be also 
provided by all NEMOSINE partners via existing contacts to other Europea n research institutes and networks. For 
examples, IPC is member of several associations which are partially related to NEMOSINE topic or could benefit 
from the results of the project, including OE -A (http://www.oe-a.org/home), AFELIM (http://www.afelim.fr/), 3D-
MID Association ( www.3d-mid.de/), and 4M ( www.4m-association.org/). Other partners´ ne tworks mentioned 
previously are:

(ACE), Fédération Internationale des Archives du Film (FIAF), AIC (American Institute of Conservation), CEPIC

Training and knowledge transfer : NEMOSINE will work to enhance the training of conservators, plastics 
application technicians and education of engineers.  In particular, the Guide included in D.6.6  delivered by the 
project will be a very useful tool to achieve this goal. As the guide wil l be published at the end of NEMOSINE, 
technical and economical evaluations for the developed prototypes will be included. This guideline will be a crucial 
tool for the potential end -users of NEMOSINE materials and technologies. NEMOSINE aims to organise 2  
workshops (anticipated at month 36 and month 48). The topic will be selected a year ahead of the workshop, 
depending on the results obtained in NEMOSINE across technical, economic and environmental areas. 
NEMOSINE will showcase the demonstrators developed  during the project and to this end the Consortium will 
analyse the feasibility to organise a workshop in the context of a major fair/exhibition in order to maximise the 
impact. 
2.2.3 Exploitation of results. 
The exploitation routes and corresponding busin ess models will be investigated in WP8. The route for 
commercialization of the results can be logically identified from the NEMOSINE WP structure and work plan, 
from the logical flow of the project activities and their clear role, as represented schematically in figure 2.1.a. 
Exploitation partner, ALINARI as expert and referent in the field conservation of photography, the image and 
communication will act as coordinator of the exploitation activities and ensure that all IP -owning partners as well 
as potential and confirmed exploitation partners will work towards a successful technology and knowledge transfer 
to ensure efficient market uptake. The role of the exploitation manager will be to assess the commercial potential of 
the results and liaise with indust rial companies to maximize their commercial use. The exploitation manager, with 
support of the members of the IPREB, composed of representatives of the appointed partners (AIMPLAS, CNRS, 
IRIS, CXD and ALINARI) , will also be responsible for establishing targeted exploitation and dissemination 
strategies, when the project outcomes reach sufficient maturity. The entire project Consortium will discuss this 
strategy and the corresponding document (PEDR) will be delivered for the preliminary and mid -term assessment 
(D8.3 & D8.4 -M12 and 30). An updated and more detailed exploitation plan will be submitted thereafter (D8.5 -
M48). 
All technologies developed by the partners will be considered for exploitation (methods, processes or materials). A 
summary of anticipated Key Exploitable Results (KER) is reported in table 2.2.d.

Intellectual Property Rights protection  activities are managed under WP8. The overall IPR strategy of the 
project is to ensure that partners are able to fully exploit their market position, involving patent protection.  
The Partners will sign a Consortium Agreement (CA) prior to the signature of the Grant Agreement with the EC 
in which all the rules for ensuring confidentiality (procedure for granting publication of the result s), owners hip 
regime and IPR issues (background included and excluded, ownership, licensing terms, etc) are detailed. Some 
previous knowledge and background are detailed in the description of each partner in section 4. The CA will be 
based on the DESCA mod el and the  Annotated Model Grant Agreement general rules. The CA will include the 
initial ‘Key Exploitable Results’ (Table 2.2.d) of the partners and patents interest list (Table 2.2.b), which will be 
the starting point for IPR protection and Exploitation Plans. 
The following three areas of activity have been identified in order to ensure proper IP management and maximize 
the impact and market relevance of the knowledge generated in the project: 
• Proper assessment of the pre -existing knowledge of the various  project partners, their potential contribution to 
the project results IP, and potential overlap of IP. In shaping the IP strategy of the consortium these will be 
assessed based on the Consortium Agreement.  
• The assessment report may be used to draft an IP  and exploitation agreement, if needed, as an integral part of 
the final exploitation plan, in line with the consortium agreement, and used as an input for the exploitation 
plans. The document will be upgraded during the project to include new results unfo reseen at the beginning of 
the developments as it is needed.  
• The overall IPR strategy annually focuses on the knowledge generated by the project, the IP rights, the 
patentability and optimal IPR protection options. Any disputes over IPRs should be settled  according to the 
consortium agreement. Legal requirements for commercialization are also explored, in particular through 
“freedom to operate” analysis as well as individual patent filing strategies and drafting of patent applications 
for the most promising project results, as it is needed. 
As described in section 3.2, the SMEs partners will have a higher percentage of participation in the results 
exploitation, so the IPR management will respect at any time the objectives established in this type of Collaborative 
Project and thus watching over SMEs interests. 
Exploitation through Standards development: Successful exploitation will only occur if the market is receptive 
to the products and processes developed in the project. After identification of the results  with stan dardisation 
potential (initially focused on enclosure and environmental quality preservation for CH, to promote the usage of 
this new storage solution in the visual imaging sector ), contacts will be made with relevant standardisation 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 37 of 110 
bodies in order to initiate, for instance a CEN workshop or contribute to existing standardisation activities in ISO. 
Some NEMOSINE partners have a strong link with standardisation bodies such as AIMPLAS, CNRS, NOVA, 
CXD and ALINARI. 
Post project execution of exploitation plan: As discussed a central aim of the NEMOSINE dissemination plan is  
to ‘prepare’ the market in order to reduce the incubation time for NEMOSINE new products and 
technologies to a maximum of 5 years after the project end,  and to provide knowledge, m ethodologies an d 
training materials that can contribute to increase competitiveness of the EU industry and workers skills in the field , 
facilitating the widespread adoption and market penetration of the developed materials and technologies.  
At the end of the project NEMOSINE technology will be at TRL6 and it is expected that a further 5 years will be 
required to achieve TRL8. Significant investment will be needed, i.e., additional budget outside of the project must 
be attracted using the patents and the tr ade secrets generated during the project and detailed in table 2.2.e.  The 
partners have resources to cover the costs needed to implement the necessary co-funding for further developing and 
marketing the results of NEMOSINE. Besides internal resources in order to support the commercial exploitation of 
the project’s results; EUREKA, national programs, investment funds (EU Investment Bank. EU Investment Fund), 
private investors and venture capital, SME instrument will be considered, as well as opportunities br ought through 
Regional Funds (ESIF), which should be possible as NEMOSINE aligns perfectly to the priorities identified under 
the RIS3 strategy for most of the Partner’s countries. To ensure that the maximum potential EU market is reached, 
the IPREB on beh alf of the  Consortium, will contact and involve Industrial Associations or SMEs in the new 
supply chain of NEMOSINE across EU thus achieving a multiplying effect and spreading the project results. 
In summary, the protection of the interest of Industry, esp ecially the SMEs, will be guaranteed as they are the 
majority represented in the various boards, and consequently an industry -driven vote will be guaranteed in all 
levels of the management structure. The existing consortium represents the complete research , development, 
manufacturing and material supply chain, thereby ensuring that the IPR protection procedure to be outlined 
within the Consortium Agreement  will be effectively managed and that the project results will be protected at 
each stage. NEMOSINE wil l result i n a n umber of innovative processes, materials, products and IPR with a high 
potential for commercialization. Therefore this consortium considers the issues of IPR management and protection 
as particularly important and the PEDR will be prepared i n order to reduce the time to market  to the minimum 
possible; although further developments will be needed after the project end to achieve TRL8. There are no known 
business agreements or commitments which may impose limitations on the exploitation. 
3. IMPLEMENTATION 
3.1. WORK PLAN - WORK PACKAGES, DELIVERABLES  
3.1.1. Overall structure of the work plan. 
NEMOSINE is a 4 -year project. It is structured into 9 workpackages, as the PERT diagram shows in the 3.1.2 
section, which are linked to promote the cooperation of par tners and to reach the target objective of NEMOSINE 
in the topic NMBP-35-2017. Each WP addresses a specific set of tasks needed to achieve sequentially the different 
goals and milestones set in the workplan. Really the workplan runs with a progressive structure from the individual 
elements (AA adsorbers and antifungals), and the modular integration of different elements: foams, nanofibers, 
sensors and wireless electronics, and barrier polymeric package. Every single has the objective to reach in the WP7 
3 real prototypes or demonstrators to validate the protective and curative performance.  
More detailed, WP1 will aims to define the packaging requirements of CH artefacts made by cell ulose derivatives. 
WP2 & WP3 are focused in the combination of different mat erials and polymeric structures to improve protection 
of CH artefacts, looking for synergetic effects. WP4 and WP5 develop the multisensors and the integration in the 
wireless RFID system and the simulation tools for predictive maintenance. WP6 will integr ate initially all the 
systems in a whole smart package  and will develop the defined prototypes and real demonstrators, as well as full 
validation in different protective applications (relevant environments). WP 7 will involves the environmental and 
economic studies, while WP8 (communication, dissemination and exploitation) and WP9 (management) will act as 
transversal workpackages, supporting the other ones. 
WP1: Definition of requirements of each selected CH artefact. WP Leader: ALINARI 
Definition of all requirements for active packaging based on specific form to be fulfilled by SSH and end -users. 
Initial 3D package concept design about the defined specifications.  
WP2: Development of protective system using MOF based on Acetic Acid absorbers and curative s ystem based 
on antifungals. WP Leader: CNRS 
Synthesis of a few existing robust hydrophobic MOFs with different structures and particle sizes for AA 
adsorption in preventive package model. Study of the fungicide effect and the efficiency of a 
disinfection/curative packages  
WP3: Acetic Acid Adsorbers and antifungals carriers integration. WP Leader: NPH 
NEMOSINE part B H2020-NMBP-35-2017 
Page 38 of 110 
MOFs will be integrated in open cell and low density foams and/or high specific surface area electrospinning 
nanofibers. The preparation of MOFs -polymer co mposites a nd se lected antifungals following different routes 
will be carried out. Efficiency of carriers will be evaluated. 
WP4: Nanostructured sensors. WP Leader: BIOSENSOR 
Development of multiscale nano -sensors to monitor the main parameters of interes t (gases) in CH deterioration 
sensing using the technologies and materials detailed in section 1.4.3. 
WP5: Wireless sensor control and development of a CH deterioration model and software. WP Leader: IRIS 
Development of a RFID system for CH packaging,  remote analysis of data received through RF and modelling 
for CH deterioration monitoring. Development of a software platform to display results from the RFID data. 
WP6: Design & fabrication of the modular packages & validation. WP Leader: AKUMPLAST 
Development of the modular multi-functional polymer package solution for CH protection, in order to validate 
the different building blocks or modules integration for the final demonstration stage. The manufacturing of the 
final prototype packages including al l the added functionalities developed in the previous WPs to protect a film 
reel of 40 cm diameter and a rectangular box 10 x 15 x 5 cm to contain photographic negatives or old 
photographs. Both will be designed to include protective functionalities (AA ad sorber, gase s barr ier, and 
sensoring) or curative functionalities (antifungal). 
WP7: Environmental, regulatory & economic analyses. WP Leader: CXD 
Evaluation of the Environmental impact of (a) the packaging and (b) its production process & supply chain. We 
will take a product life cycle approach). Techno -economic analysis, to optimise (minimise) costs; and optimise 
revenue opportunities. 
WP8: IPR protection, Technology Transfer, Business Model, Communication and Dissemination. WP Leader: 
ALINARI 
Complete IPR protec tion, dissemination and technology transfer activities to ensure the full exploitation of the 
innovations and scientific results will be carried out in this work -package. A Plan for the Exploitation and 
Dissemination of Results (PEDR) will be elaborated, including the Dissemination Plan and the Business Plan. 
WP9: Project Management, WP Leader AIMPLAS 
Project’s activity coordination, efficient Grant management (resources optimization), communication with the 
EC, Risk Management.

3.1.4. Technical Risks and contingency plans.  
The project team has carefully considered the technical risks associated with this project, summarizing the potential 
risks, their likelihood and imp act, and the actions which will be taken to mitigate them. Significant risks have 
therefore been addressed through the work programme and partnership to ensure that the outcomes of the project 
are achievable ( Table 3.3a: Main technical risks and contingency plans ). The experience of all partners in their 
respective fields and a continuous co -ordination and risk assessment (T 9.2) will make possible to overcome or 
minimize potential problems if they arise. In the current status, the following risks could be identified.

The amounts of MOFs that can be supported in the polyurethane foam

WP3 
After being supported in the foam or fibers, the MOF particles will be 
covered by a thin film o f polymer. This may a ct as a diffusion barrier 
which vapours need to permeate to access the MOFs, slowing the 
overall adsorption process. An alternative approach is to squeeze the 
final composite  (foam or fibers)  to slightly crush the MOF pellets 
and/or to rupture of the thin layer covering the particles or to cut the 
composites in thin slices (1 to 5 cm) to rupture of the thin layer 
covering the pellets. These These alternatives were already successful 
tested for activated carbon pellets supported in PUR f oams, and thus 
the risk is significantly reduced if these alternative approaches need to 
be used. Increasing the concentration bath for dip coating process or 
activating the surface by plasma to increase MOF adsorption.

3.2 MANAGEMENT STRUCTURE, MILESTONES AND PROCEDURES  
The Consortium of NEMOSINE 
will be coord inated by Partner 
AIMPLAS. The project 
management structure has been 
conceived to ensure the 
competent industrial, scientific 
and business management of 
NEMOSINE project and to 
enable efficient and effe ctive 
integration and communication 
throughout the man agement 
chain. NEMOSINE project 
success will be strongly based on 
the close interaction and 
equilibrated partnership of SMEs 
 
Figure 3.2.a Project Management Structure. 

NEMOSINE part B H2020 NMBP-35-2017 
 
Page 43 of 109 
 
(̴50%), research centers, and SSH 
institutions50.  
This ma nagement structure has been implemented successfu lly in similar EU Projects coordinated by Partner  
AIMPLAS (e.g. FP7 BRIGIT, BUGWORKERS and BISIGODOS, and H2020 JOSPEL, URBANREC and DAFIA), 
and as such,  has been adopted by the NEMOSINE Consortium with the latest improvements suggested by 
H2020. A schemat ic representation of the management structure of NEMOSINE is shown in Figure 3.2.a.  The 
project management structure is clearly industry and SSH driven a s an RTD directly involved in the proposal core 
topic, OEAW, chairs the General Assembly (GA). Furtherm ore, another Social Scienci e and Humanity (SSH) 
organization, a large company, CXD chairs the Executive Board (EB) and the SSH Public body -OTHER ALINARI 
chairs the IPR, Dissemination & Exploitation Board (IP REB). Moreover, there are 6 SMEs with R&D capacit ies. 
All boards have a majority representation of In dustrial Partners as described below. An overview of the governance 
structure and decision -making pro cess is also detailed below. The composition of the bo ards a nd the decision 
making mechanisms have been  designed in order to ensure that all decisions are taken in accordance with the 
Industrial commercial interests, and SME’s interests in particular, and also providing a relevant role to the SSH 
partners, as a direct way to reach the potential future clients of the NEMOSINE products.  
The structure adopted is particularly business like and highly end -user/clients oriented (as opposed to 
bureaucratic) to en sure that NEMOSINE is run as a “commercially” orientat ed pro ject with a very clear 
business focus on th e SSH stakeholders and citizens, in general. Neverth eless, there is the opportunity for all 
partners to express their opinion and canvas support through the General Assembly (GA) which will meet at least 
twice a y ear to ratify progress and decisions made b y the management bodies. The GA has the ultimate dec ision 
making power in the Consortium.  
Decision –Making mechanisms: All Boards and Committees will typically meet at least twice per year. Any group 
will deliberate and decide validly provided a majority of its members are present or represented and each m ember 
will have one vote with the Chairperson having a casting vote if required. Decisions will be ta ken by a majority of 
two-thirds of the votes of the me mbers present and the members that have delegated  their vote. General Assembly 
meetings, meetings inv olving industrial demonstration or key technical meetings will be face -to-face, conference 
calls will be also encouraged. All the partners have the responsibilities described below as a result of taking p art in 
a specific decision making body. In all of them, the SME and Industrial participants will have the highest level 
of decision-making competency (majority voting). 
The General Assembly (GA) consists of 16 representatives (one per partner), and is chaired by OEAW. The GA is 
the ultimate decision-making and arbitration body of the Consortium (the final and highest authority in the project). 
However, it delegates short -term decisions -making actions to the Executive Board (EB). Such decisions do 
however re quire subsequent acceptance by the GA. The GA will d ecide on matters relating to: a) The political 
strategic and economic orientation of the Project, its  objectives, definition and subsequent modifications, including 
the shift of budget of the Project. b) Actions towards defaulting parties, including their substitution. c) The 
nomination and election of EB members. d) The acceptance & exclusion of new part ies or affiliates in the ECGA 
and in the Consortium Ag reement. e) The Consortium Agreement and its Anne xes. f) Description of Work, 
subsequent Project Impl ementation Plan and ECGA, including proposals and modifications. g) Ultimate approval 
of IPR Policies & Exploitation Plans proposed by the IPREB. 
The Executive Board (EB) is responsible for the strategic and political guidance of the Project. It is composed of 
one representative of each one of the 16 partners . CXD will chair the EB. The responsibilities of the  EB 
include: Overall guidance & supervision over strategic, political, economic & operational day -to-day issues 
regarding the Project. Definition, app roval and fulfilment of Project objectives. Scientific and Technological 
Quality Assessment. Definiti on and implementation of risk management methodology a t all levels (financial, 
technical and administrative). Evaluation of results and definition of level s for dissemination relating to all kind of 
information and reports. Conflict Resolution. Constitutio n and administration of the funding. Presentation of t he 
taken decisions to the GA periodically. 
The EB will decide on matters relating to: The shift of ta sks and responsibilities and budget of the Project. The 
regulations governing the decision -making and  operational procedures of the EB and other Project bo dies. The 
method of payment and management proced ures of the Community’s financial contribution. Requ ests for 
subcontracting, within the context of the Project. The actions to be taken in accordance wit h the evaluation of 
 
 
50 Note that CNRS & OEAW partners have double role, both as RO and SSH, due to their huge influence in the CH -audiovisual field. For the calcutaions of their weight in the

results obtained. The reporting, c ontrolling and auditing procedures concerning the  Project. The validation of 
reports and Project Deli verables to be submitted to the EC within the EC reporting activity together with annual 
validation of the realised expenditure in accordance with the budget of the Project. 
The Technical Management Commi ttee (TMC) is the body responsible for ensuring the overall technical co -
ordination of the Project work, in accordance with the Work Programme, subsequen t Implementation Plan, and EB 
decisions, at Scientific , Tech nical, Financial and Administrative level. The TMC’s main responsibilities also 
include: ensuri ng co -ordination between WPs, facilitating the take -up of research results, supervision of the 
implementation of the EB decisions, and the assessment of Pr oject results. The TMC, Chaired by CNRS  will be 
composed by the WP Leaders: ALINARI (WP1), CNRS (WP2) , NPH (WP3), BIOSENSOR (WP4), IRIS (WP5),, 
AKUMPLAST (WP6), CXD (WP7), ALINARI (WP8) and AIMPLAS (WP9). 
The TMC will be responsible for: Ensuring the i mplementation of the decisions taken by the EB at W P level; 
Making proposals to the EB for the re -allocation of material, financial and human resources, tasks and 
responsibilities. Preparing deliverable s & other information requested by the EB, based on re ports by the WP 
Leaders. Validating and seeking EB approval for subcontracting. Ensuring co -ordination between WPs facilitating 
the take-up of research results in the demonstration activities. Assisting  WP leaders on day to day management. 
Monitoring the projects technical progress against the identified technical risks, as described in T9.2. 
The TMC will convene meetings with the Work Package Leaders at least quarterly (typically 2 face -to-face 
meetings and 2 conference call meetings) and if applicable wit h the EB, for purposes of co -ordination and 
management. Where the TMC cannot settle decision making disputes, the decision shall be taken in the EB.  
The Work Package Leaders (WPL) , as identified above will report and be accountable to the TMC. The specifi c 
WPL will be responsible for their own WP organizational arrangements, work procedures, day-to-day management 
and time schedule, providing that such arrangements, work procedures and time schedule do n ot conflict with the 
ECGA, the Consortium Agreement, t he Description of Work, subsequent Implementation P lans, or requests and 
other provisions made by the app ropriate bodies within the Consortium or the EC. Meetings of a specific WP will 
be convened at le ast quarterly, either face -to-face or by conference/vi deo call. Extraordinary Meetings shall be: a) 
Called in and convened by the corresponding WP Leader; or b) by the TMC Chairperson. 
The Project Coordinator (AIMPLAS) is the intermediate for communication between the Consortium and the EC 
and shall report an d be a ccountable to the EB and the GA. The Coordina tor is in charge of the financial and 
administrative management (WP9) of the Project. The Coordinator will submit for EB validation, the reports which 
shall be submitted to EC within the EC reporting activ ity. The reports covering project deliverables, sup porting 
documents and audit certificates will be provi ded to the Coordinator by the TMC. For the avoidance of any doubt, 
the Co-ordinator has the capac ity of representation of the consortium before the Com mission. The Co -ordinator 
undertakes to keep the Jo int Funds allocated by the EU Grant Agreement or by bu dget in accordance with the 
provisions which will be defined in the Consortium Agreement and in t he Grant Agreement and decisions from the 
appropriate bodies. The main coordinators responsibilities will include:  
a) Periodic Reporting: the project coordinator will be responsible for ensuring the collation and timely submission 
of the contractual repor ts required by the EC, always according to the EC repo rting requirements for the H2020 
Programme. With regards to the project periodic reports, the project man ager’s activities shall include: the creation 
of report /information gathering templates, providi ng support to the project consortium and enabling each  project 
partner to undertake their responsibilities for the provision of information to complete such reports and making sure 
that each partner is made aware of the deadlines for the timely delivery of any required information. Project reports 
will be sub mitted to the EC on due time, including copies of t he minutes, presentations given by partners and 
additional information. b) Periodic Commission Questionnaires: if the Commission requires a number of 
periodic questionnaires, the Project Co-ordinator will be in charge of coordinating the completion and rep orting of 
these questionnaires. c) To ensure the verif ication and submission of the project deliverable reports: all 
deliverable reports have to be ver ified initially by the EB before submission to the pro ject coordinator, who will 
ensure that they are according to the EC requirements and submitted timely. d) Coordination of the Periodic and 
Review Project Meetings: the project coordinator will assume re sponsibility for the organization of those 
meetings, taking into account the attendance of the EC representative(s) and the independent reviewer(s) appointed 
by the EC. The project coordinator will coordinate: the meeting venue, agenda, minutes and other l ogistical 
arrangements, in cooperation with the hosting Partner. e) Collection of Certificates on Financial Statements: the 
project coordinator will ensure tha t all Partners who are required to provide a CFS, provide them in a timely 
manner at the end of t he Project. f) Reporting and Payment of Project Financ ing: assuming the role of project 
banker and taking responsibility for holding and payment of the project  funds in accordance with the agreement of 
the General Assembly and the Consortium Agreement. g) Additional responsibilities of the project coordinator  
NEMOSINE part B H2020 NMBP-35-2017 
 
Page 45 of 109 
 
will include: coordination for the updating and si gnature of the project Consortium Agreement and Contra ct 
amendments (when required); to provide a platform for communication between the EC and the pro ject 
consortium/ management structure; to provide supp ort and information to the project consortium in fu lfilment of 
the project contract and EC requirements. 
The representation of the Social Science Humanities bodies (i.e. organisms devoted to the Cultura l Heritage 
linked to NEMOSINE) is essential to ensure the proper uptake of the new products in the market. Then, not 
only the SMEs and Industrial Partners, but  also those SSH bodies will own the ultimate decision making in 
accordance with the organizationa l structure. As detailed above, all Consortium bodies have a  majority of 
Industrial and SSH Partners (12 out of 16), thus, in the end, the decisions are taken by majority voting, 
guaranteeing that the participating Industries needs and requirements, and SS H demands (as representatives of the 
end-users/customers) ar e fulfilled and consequently, that the result s of the project will be for the benefit of the 
sectors involved in the NEMOSINE value chain.  
From the Technical point of view, the Project Co -ordinator, delegating day to day work to the defined 
Management Bod ies, will monitor the overall progress of the  Project in all its aspects, with specific 
responsibilities in this regard for d evelopment of the Technical Report Procedures and the Technical Progres s 
Monitoring and templates for technical activities.  
The IPR, Dissemination & Exploitation Board  (IPREB) will be chaired by partner ALINARI, and the rest of 
Members chosen to represent the consortium ( AIMPLAS, CNRS, IRIS, CXD). They  are key partners who  are 
involved in the innovation and IPR generation and  protection of key technologies for their companies  as well as 
commercialization. IPREB will propose the IPR Policy and the Action Plan for the Exploitation of project results to 
the EB and GA. The IPRE B will be responsible for the preparation, monitoring and up dating of the list of 
exploitable results and innovations that will be used to monitor the progress and achievements of the project and to 
assess the Plan for the Exploitation and Dissemination of  Results (PEDR, including both the Dissemination and 
Business Plan). The IPREB will look to increase the IP  protection and ownership awareness and implementation,  
supported by training activities given by the IPR helpdesk and other EC support services needed. 
Finally, a stakeholders´ committee (made up of representatives of SHH partners) has been appointed as a  way to 
have a closer contact with the potential end -users/key external partners that can contribute to spread the products´ 
uptake once ready to be commercialized. The SSH NEMOSINE partners have a n outstanding list of useful 
contacts, apart from the Letters of Support attached.  
In summary, the protection of the interest of the End-users and Industry will be guaranteed as they are the majority 
represented in the various boards, and consequently a commerc ial industry-driven vote will be guaranteed in all 
levels of the management structure, allowing a day-to-day management as in a processing chain at industrial level, 
with protection of the interests of SMEs and SSH entities and innovations. 
Appropriateness of the organisational structure and decision-making mechanisms. 
As mentioned above, the project management structure has been replicated from that used in FP7 and H2020 
projects coordinated by AIMPLAS. This structure has been proven to be agile and has be en successful in properly 
managing projects of a similar nature to NEMOSINE, solving conflicts and overcoming hurdles for their successful 
completion. In addition, strong cooperation already exists among the majority of NEMOSINE Partners within FP6, 
FP7 or  H2020 projects, with an open management and cooperat ive approach which benefits from the relevant 
experience of all Partners. Moreover, the project partnership is highly complementary and industry driv en; each 
Partner with sound experience in their respec tive fields of work, have clear objectives and respon sibility of tasks, 
and each of them fully understands a nd is highly committed to exploit the project outcomes, ensuring that the high 
degree of cooperation achieved already during proposal preparation will continue during project execution. 
Innovation Mana gement: the IPREB will implement the Innovation Management strategy  developed within 
NEMOSINE. All NEMOSINE’s technologies can be exploited by a relevant number of additional applications by 
modification/adaptation of MOFs, sensors, or nanofibers. The Partners complementarities along the value chain and 
their highly innovative nature will foster cross -fertilisation and boost innovation within the proje ct, simply by the 
collaborative execution of the work plan. In addition, the project will constantly look f or internal and external 
opportunities in order to furt her promote innovation. The project will use the dissemination and business plan in 
order to d etect needs of potential customers and future end -users of t he results and will proactively look for 
feedback from all stakeholders, entities and organisations (i ndustrial platforms, public authorities, standard setters) 
that can be useful to improve NEMOSINE results, modifying accordingly the work plan if de emed u seful. 
Similarly, the project partners will communicate internally the project development, fostering constructive criticism 
and feedback from staff, engineers, and designers and in particular man agers. All this feedback will be gathered by 
the IPREB and discussed during the GA meetings to agree possible modifications of the workplan if improvements 
NEMOSINE part B H2020 NMBP-35-2017

in the results can occur resulting from this innovation management strategy
3.3 CONSORTIUM AS A WHOLE  
3.3.1 Overall description: adequacy, complementarities, representativity of the value chain and synergies.  
NEMOSINE consortium has a well -balanced composition. The NEMOSINE consortium brings together a wealth 
of expertise and resources within the areas, in cluding p artners that propose  the best solutions to ma ximize the 
environmentally friendly conservation of O RIGINAL works, i.e. films, audios, slides, and photogra phs. The 
presence of main actors in the whole value chain demonstrates the critical mass of co mplimentary resources that 
will enable the NEMOSINE pr oject to achieve its targeted societal, industrial, a nd scientific breakthroughs and 
commercial success. Each partner has a clearly defined role within the project and will contribute specific expertise 
that will enable the project success. RTD Partners (AIMPLAS, CNRS, IST, NOVA, IPC and OEAW) have the 
necessary research expertise and will provide support to the  partners to achieve their objectives . They will adapt 
and validate the active substances to p rotect or cure the CH artefacts, as well as, desig n the whole smart package.

(CXD), whose main aim is the integration of all the active elements prepared by research cente rs in the initial 
workpackages and the development of final 3 prototypes able to work in real environments.

To obtain the complementary range of expertise  and the critical mass needed (both in human and finan cial terms), 
it is necessary to bring together, companies and ROs representing the entire supply chain and R &D areas, working 
in close cooperation to solve a common problem, which cannot be found within  a single EU Region, requiring the 
integration of resources from across EU.  
NEMOSINE partnership is composed by  16 organizations from 10 EU countries, having the  required pan EU 
approach essential for achieving the objectives of the project since it is re quired to address the EU social and 
Industry needs in the fi eld with a wide EU perspective. Furthermore, to ensu re that the long -term commercial 
success of the NEMOSINE results, it is important that the project innovation and research activities are undert aken 
with a strong knowledge of the different industri al sectors addressed as well as through all the types of e nd-users 
focused on (based on the 3 levels of pack age and the different clients linked to each of them). The Consortium 
therefore ensures the pa rticipation of different EU regions, whose roles withi n the project are clearly defined and 
represent strategica lly important regional objectives, which will addr ess t he overall objectives of enhancing 
European industrial competitiveness, for instance with  RIS3 smart specialisation strategies, providing a clear EU 
added value. 
3.3.2 Industrial/Commercial involvement to ensure exploitation of the results.  
NEMOSINE project clearly has a number of benefits for the involved SME as explained in detail along the  
proposal. It enables the transfer and market replication of the new materials/components for manufacturing the new 
smart conservation package, with improved perf ormance, cost/quality ratio, and sustainability and that contributes 
to the developed the well-defined and high market three types of smart package;  supporting the take-up of the new 
advanced manufacturing materials and technologies and becoming a source o f information, training and technical / 
regulatory support. Besides, NEMOSINE will create a ne w and more open market/supply chain for the materials,  
technologies and sales as previous figures shows under Section 2. 
The involvement of all the participants d uring and after the end of the project, in order to strengthen the industrial 
and commercial e xploitation, is a key aspect of the consortium relatio nship, implemented through the innovation 
and IPR manageme nt strategies resulting in the Business Plan inclu ded i n the Final PEDR (Plan for the 
Exploitation and Dissemination of the Results). 
During the project. Throughout the life of the project, all proj ect partners will be responsible for updating the 
project ‘Plan for the Exploitation and Dissemination of Re sults’. Dissemination will target ‘take-up’ actions within 
EU Local Authorities -Public Bodies, Stakeholders, SMEs and End -Users to promote the growt h of t he materials 
and technologies developed into new and  existing market sectors; and to encourage SME par ticipation within the 
NEMOSINE supply chain. Publication and dissemination of project knowledg e and results will be conducted on 
agreement between the consortium partners, led by the IPREB chaired by ALINARI ensuring that the SMEs and 
industry interests are not only taken into account but are the real drivers for the exploitation strategy. Managed by

Industrial participation is very strong in this project. The conso rtium includes six + one industry partners (6 SMEs  
+ 1 large company, almost half of the consortium), with multiple and complementary technologi cal, research and 
business expertise, covering the ful l spec trum of the activities proposed in NEMOSINE. They ar e dynamic 
enterprises with an active intention and  outlook to expand their product/service portfolio into new markets. All 
project industrial pa rtners planning to directly capitalize on the NEMOSINE  results as we explain in detail in 
impact section. The geographical dispersion of the industrial partners e nsures that we cover an high proportion of 
European markets.

for NEMOSINE meetings assistance is 7,600 €, assuming that one person per partner attends. Please no te that, 
based on partners´previous experiences, these costs also include a buffer for other possible type of meetings , if 
applicable, when nececcary along the project (e.g. technical meetings, visits among specific partners,etc).

4. MEMBERS OF THE CONSORTIUM 
4.1. PARTICIPANTS (APPLICANTS). 
PARTNER 1 
Full name : AIMPLAS -Asociación de Investigación de 
Materiales Plásticos y Conexas (AIMPLAS) 
Web page: www.aimplas.es 
Country: Spain  
Type: RO 
  
Brief description of the organization: AIMPLAS, Technological Institute of Plastics located in Valencia, is a 
private, non -profit Association with more than 500 associated companies created in 1990. AIMPLAS is 
formed by +120 highly skilled professional , m ore than 65% with a Masters, Engineering or equivalent 
degree in Chemistry, polymer engineering, materials engineering or equivalent, including 15 PhD.  
AIMPLAS’ fields of work are related to technological research and development on thermoplastic and 
thermosetting plastic materials & products, its transformation processes and their recyclability and 
sustainability. AIMPLAS generates new knowledge and technologies that can be transferred to companies 
in order to help them to increase their effectiveness and competitiveness. 
AIMPLAS has a broad expertise in the fields of recycling, compatibilization, reactive extrusion, biopolymers 
and renewable source materials, special assisted processing technologies and nanocomposites, gained 
during the last years in t he frame of EU and national projects. Nowadays, AIMPLAS is involved in more 
than 25 European projects and has participated in 77 projects in FP5, FP6, FP7, LIFE+, CIP -EcoInnovation 
EU Programmes, among others, coordinating 27 of them. At National and Regio nal levels A IMPLAS 
participates in around 100 projects yearly.  
AIMPLAS, as RO is focused to help companies in the plastic sector to develop new products and increase 
their competitiveness through innovation, has more than 20 pilot plants representing the most relevant 
polymer/plastics/composites production technologies present in the industry nowadays and has state -of-
the art test facilities for chemical, optical, morphological, mechanical and physical characterisation. These 
pilot lines and laboratories a re used by many customer’s every year allowing them to test new materials, 
optimize production processes and launch new products to the market, supported by AIMPLAS technical 
staff, resulting in more than 5000 assays, 170 technical assessments and 120 skills training actions to more 
than 1500 clients per year. AIMPLAS has state -of-the-art 8500 m 2 facilities, including thermoplastics and 
thermoset pilot plants, analysis and testing laboratories (physical -mechanical, chemical, packaging, 
automotive and construction) and training areas.  
Role in the Project:  
Project coordinator (WP9). Support industrial partners to adapt the materials development to obtain the 
demo packages at pilot plant Level.  Development of nanofibers carriers, antifungal composites, 
incorporation of MOFs into open cell foams at lab scale. Contribution to communication, dissemination, 
exploitation, business plan, LCA, LCC, and other related activities. Regulatory analysis. 
Scientific team:  
Dr. Adolfo Benedito (M) , PhD degree in Chemistry by the University of Valencia, focusing on ABS 
copolymer degradation and recycling capabilities. Since Mars 2001, he has been working at AIMPLAS as 
head of Compounding department until 2009 and currently as Head of the Materials Research 
Department. He has been the main technical responsible of several EU -research and national projects, as 
well as author and co -author of several papers, patents and book chapters focused on nanotechnology 
applied to polymeric materials. 
Mr. Serafín Garcia , Engineer, responsi ble for t he Design and Injection department since 2004.  
He has wide experience in a multidisciplinary approach to find integrated and comprehensive  
solutions for the plastic sector on processing optimization. He is expert in plastic materials with or without 
NEMOSINE part B H2020 NMBP-35-2017

reinforcements. He is also responsible on research activities focused in Additive Manufacturing and 
Industry 4.0 at AIMPLAS. 
Dr. Alba María Ortiz Álvarez (female) , European PhD in chemistry by the Universidad de Alcalá, Madrid 
(December 2012), working i n AIMPLAS as PhD researcher in the chemical laboratory since 2013. Sh e has 
been involved in several national and international research projects  focused in different areas such as 
synthesis of new polymers, nanotechnology, materials from renewable resource s a nd coatings with 
enhanced properties, and so on. Moreover, she has being involved in the technical work of on Food 
contact plastics as well as Pharmacopoeia. Before joining AIMPLAS, she worked at the Universidad de

new enlarged-palladium complexes as recoverable catalysts by nanofiltration techniques, contributing in 
international peer-reviewed journals and in national and international conference pap ers in the field of 
catalysis, dendrimers and organometallic chemistry. 
Mrs. Raquel Giner (F), Degree in Chemical Sciences by the University of Valencia (Spain) in 2000. Working

Brief description of the organization: 
Partner 2: CNRS 
The National Center for Scientific Research, or CNRS, is a public organization under the responsibility of the 
French Ministry of Education and Research. It aims to: 
• Evaluate and carry out all research  capable of advancing knowledge and bringing social, cultural, 
and economic benefits for society. 
• Contribute to the promotion and application of research results. 
• Develop scientific information. 
• Support research training. 
• Participate in the analysis of the  national and international scientific climate and its potential for 
evolution in order to develop a national policy. 
CNRS laboratories (or research units) are located throughout France, and employ a large body of tenured 
researchers, engineers, and support staff. 
Partner 2a : Institute of Porous Materials from Paris (IMAP) 
CNRS-Versailles. The CNRS-IMAP group led by C. Serre (DR-CNRS), created end of 2016 and initially located 
at the Institut Lavoisier de Versailles (France), is a world leader in the synth esis, structural characterization 
and applications of porous MOF solids with more than two hundreds reported new porous solids within 
the last decade. It has developed a well -established expertise in the hydro/solvothermal synthesis and 
structure determination using when required computer modelling, of new porous MOFs. This know -how 
has been developed in conjunction with the understanding of their formation mechanism through the 
development of in or ex -situ studies (solid state NMR, X -ray diffraction...) an d t he identification of the 
inorganic or hybrid building units present in solution. The group also developed a large network of french 
or foreign collaborations to deeply characterize these hybrid solids (in -situ IR, Raman and Mössbauer 
spectroscopies, mol ecular simulation...) as well as study their properties in several strategic and/or 
societal domains of application (green-house gas sorption liquids phase separation, magnetism, lithium ion 
insertion, drug delivery, thin films...). This group has also acqu ired skills in the functionalization of MOFs 
nanoparticles by polymers, the synthesis of MOFs -polymer membranes or MOFs -graphene-oxide 
composites for different applications including biomedicine or gas separation. IMAP possesses many 
equipments related to the synthesis of MOFs, from their miniutarized (g scale, high -throughput) to large 
scale synthesis (Kg), to their structural (powder diffractometers (combinatorial, high resolution, 
temperature)) or physico-chemical characterization (thermogravimetric analysis, sorption porosimeters, IR 
NEMOSINE part B H2020 NMBP-35-2017 
 
Page 57 of 109 
 
spectrometer…). This also includes an access to a wide range of characterization platforms at ENS or ESPCI 
(SEM-FEG equipped with EDX, TEM, liquid phase NMR…). Shaping instruments will be soon available 
(2017) at IMAP to produce granules or extrudates of MOFs up to the 100 g scale. 
Role in the Project: 
In this project the Institute of Porous Materials, based on the above-mentioned expertise, will be in charge 
of : 
• Synthesis and characterization of MOFs able to adsorb selectively VOCs 
The IMAP will select or design the most appropriate MOFs systems that are able to absorb selectively 
VOCs (e.g. acetic acid) in the presence of moisture. IMAP will produce these MOFs at different scales or 
bearing various particle shapes, depending on the requirements from the project. The group will also carry 
out the physico-chemical characterization of MOFs micro or nano-particles (powder, shaped particles). 
• Preparation of MOFs-polymers packages or fibers 
The IMAP will assist partners for the preparation of the MOFs-polymers packages (electrospinning, foams). 
To enhance the compatibility between the MOFs particles and the polymers, surface functionalised MOFs 
particles might be prepared based on the strong know-how of the team in this field. 
Scientific team: 
Dr.  Christian Serre 
C. SERRE (DR CNRS, 46 years old, h index=74, >260 articles) (M) is a research director at ESPCI and got his 
PhD in Inorganic chemistry in 1999 (Versailles, France). Christian is one of the world leader in the 
synthesis, structural determination and application of porous MOF solids. He has an extensive experience 
in EU and national project coordination including an ERC Starting Grant (BioMOFs, 2008 -2013) and two 
FP6 or FP7 projects. He is currently workpackage leader of four  other ongoing FP7 EU projects ( M4CO2, 
FP7-608490, Sotherco, FP7 -295775)), HeteroMOFs (IF -H2020, 2015 -2017) and Gramofon (H2020, 2016 -
2019). He is head of the IMAP group at Paris Versailles. CS has received the bronze medal of CNRS in 2006, 
the French chemical society solid state chemistry award in 2010 and in 2016 the Berthelot medal and the 
Prix Fondé par l’Etat from the French academy of sciences. His role in this project will be related to the 
synthesis and characterization of MOFs and MOFs-polymers composites. 
Dr. Farid Nouar 
F. NOUAR (CNRS Research Engineer, 41 years old) (M) is a research engineer at IMAP and got is PhD in 
Inorganic chemistry/material science in 2010 (Tampa, USA). F. Nouar has been involved in several national 
(ANR, industrial collaborations) or EU projects from the team (Macademia, M4CO 2 and Gramofon) dealing 
with the synthesis and scale -up of MOFs for the capture of gases or vapors. He will be in charge in the 
Nemosine project of the synthesis optimisation, scale-up and shaping of MOFs.

Relevant Projects: 
 
Partner 2c : CRC, Centre de Recherche sur la Conservation 
The CRC is a CNRS research unit, founded in 1963, under the umbrella of the National council of scientific 
research (CNRS : USR 3224), the French Ministry of Culture and the National museum of Natural history. 
CRC is involved in research to improve the conservation and preservation of heritage goods artifacts from 
museums and archival collections to monuments. CRC is playing a role in the training and the education of 
scientists, conservators and curators. A staff of 40 heritage scientists and technicians with a background in 
chemistry, physics or microbiology, endeavor to develop the techniques of preserving museum artefacts in 
their original state for as long as possible. In order to fulfill these goals, the CRC is equipped with analytical 
tools such as high performance liquid chromatography (HPLC, SEC-MALS, LC-MS), 2D gas chromatography/ 
Mass spectrometry (2D -GC/MS), UV-visible spectrometry, Fourier transform infrared spectroscopy (FTIR), 
RAMAN micro spectroscopy, FORS, differential scanning calorimetry (DSC), VNIR Hyperspectral Imaging, 
MEB and access to analytical platforms and  synchrotron facilities  (such as Soleil). CRC perfo rms 
accelerated ageing in climate chambers to evaluate the influence of temperature, light and pollutants on 
the deterioration process of these materials (thermal ageing, light ageing, pollution ageing). These 
apparatus permitted the CRC to take part to Eu ropean research projects on the effect of pollution on 
paper, leather and parchment or videotapes (STEP, MAP, IDAP, PRESTOSPACE). Within the LiDo project, 
CRC has introduced the Lightcheck light dosimeter or coordination the POPART for the preservation of 
Synthetic polymers in cultural heritage? 
The Center has an educational position, which not only includes the teaching of university students but 
also permanent training for curators and conservators. The CRC is in contact with similar foreign 
organizations through its participation in different international organizations such as the ICCROM and the 
Committee of Conservation of the ICOM (International Council of Museums).

Role in the Project: 
In this project the CRC will focus on the efficiency of those sm art packaging in real condition of use in 
archives and museums. 
• Assessment of efficiency for acidic traps 
Once the different smart packages/enclosures are manufactured, the CRC will assess their ability and 
effectiveness to adsorb acidic gases produced by cellulose ester derivatives in different conditions of 
temperature and humidity. While the smart package made on synthetic polymer packages are produced, 
the CRC will prepare sheet of cellulosic substrate embedded with different adsorbants such as zeolithe s, 
active charcoal and MOFs. The VOC adsorption of the different packages will be compared in term of 
efficiency, as soon as the smart packaging are made available by the industrial partners, the same 
assessment will be perform. 
• Assessment of fungistatic properties 
Once packagings with encapsulated of peptides antifungals and other volatile substances are successfully 
produced by industrial partners, the CRC will test their fungistatic effect on contaminated photographs 
(with from the 19th and 20 centuries) in regular condition of used. 
• Assessment of risks 
The standardized photographic activity test will be applied to ensure that those smart packaging materials 
will not induce any damages on photographs. Long term behaviour of those packages will be tested 
through thermal and light ageing. 
Scientific team:  
Dr. Bertrand LAVEDRINE  (M)   got a Master degree in organic chemistry at Pierre and Marie Curie 
University and received the doctoral degree from the University of Paris I Panthéon -Sorbonne. He his 
professor at the National Museum of Natural History and since 1998 head of the “Centre de recherche sur 
la conservation” (CRC) - From 2004 to 2007, he was appointed as the director of the conservation training 
programme at University of Paris I. He has authored n umerous papers and books on preventive 
conservation of audio -visual collections and preservation of modern and contemporary art materials. 
Some of those books are now available in French, English, Spanish, Russian and Vietnamese. Bertrand 
Lavédrine has rec eived the european prize for innovation for conservation innovation (for a passive light 
dosimeter), the Kraszna -Krauz Photography Book award for his book “ A Guide to the Preventive 
Conservation of Photographs Collections. (Los-Angeles publish by J. Paul Getty Trust. 2003). He his teaching 
collection preservation and conservation science at the university of Paris I, the Ecoel du Louvre, the 
National Institute for Heritage (INP) where he is coordinating science programme.  He is involved in some 
international initiatives funded by the Mellon and/or the Getty foundation such as MEPPI project in 
Middle East, the Hermitage initiative or the ICCROM training programmes such as COLLASIA or SOIMA. 
 Dr. Anne -Laurence DUPONT (F)  is researcher at CNRS. She completed a  MSc in Biochemistry at the 
University of Montpellier in 1988, graduated from the Art Conservation Master’s program from the 
University Paris-Sorbonne in 1994, and received a PhD in Chemistry from the University of Amsterdam in 
2003. She obtained the Habil itation in 2014. Since 2001 she is Research Scientist at Centre de Recherche 
sur la Conservation des Collections (CRC, Muséum National d’Histoire Naturelle, Sorbonne Universités) 
where she in charge of the Paper and Cellulose section. Her current research focuses on the 
characterization and diagnostic methods of the degradation of cellulose and paper, on the impact of the 
indoor environment on cellulosic artefacts and its modelisation, and on developing new treatment 
methodologies for the long -term stabiliz ation of paper. She has authored and co -authored over 75

Brief description of the organization : Instituto Superior Técnico (IST) is t he largest and most reputed 
school of Engineering, Science and Technology in Portugal. Since its creation in 1911, IST’s mission is to 
contribute to the development of society by providing top quality higher education, at undergraduate and 
postgraduate levels, as well as developing Research, Development and Innovation (RD&I) activities to allow 
it to provide teaching in line with the highest international standards. 
IST is involved with some of the most prestigious RD&I and technology transfer institutions in Portugal, 
with remarkable impact internationally in many scientific and technological domains. Internationalization 
has been defined as a key strategic goal over the past few years with increasing number of international 
students and staff as well as an  increasing participation in international academic networks and 
establishment of several double degree programs in both MSc and PhD levels. This way, IST contributes to 
the development of the students’ educational level, offering them several opportunitie s to participate in 
international research networks, approaching scientific cooperation and multicultural experience, and 
motivating innovation and entrepreneurship. 
Role in the Project: Assessment of adsorbers regarding their capacity & kinetics of remova l organic compounds.

Scientific team:  
Prof. Moisés L. Pinto (M)  got his Ph.D. in Chemistry (Physical Chemistry), at the end of 2005, at the

Compounds by Gas-Solid Adsorption”. After obtaining the Ph.D., he also worked for the chemical industry 
as an external consultant and as manager of R&D laboratories. He has been involved in several R&D  
projects for the development and application of adsorbent materials in purification of gas mixtures, gas 
storage and capture of volatile organic compounds and gases. He is an expert in the characterization of 
nanoporous materials for adsorption applications. From the 2014, he is Assistant Professor at the Chemical

Brief description of the organization:  
Founded in 1977, the Faculty of Sciences and Technology of NOVA University of Lisbon (FCT NOVA) is one 
of the most prestigious Portuguese and Europ ean engineering and science public schools. It is engaged in 
extensive research activity involving around 600 PhD students of the total enrolment of more than 8900 
students.  
FCT NOVA partners with foreign universities such as the Massachusetts Institute o f Technology (MIT), the 
Carnegie Mellon University (CMU) and the University of Texas at Austin (UTAustin) to offer some of its 
advanced study programs, pioneers nationwide. FCT NOVA has a broad expertise in cutting edge R&D+I 
due to its multidisciplinary n ature and strong experience in fundamental and applied research projects in

several areas, ranging from materials, environment and biotechnologies to conservation and restoration. 
The entrepreneurial drive of the students and graduates of FCT NOVA, greatly  potentiated by the 
curricular profile of school, has led to many successful spin-offs that transfer knowledge to the market and 
help create value and social impact. 
With a total of 630 academic staff (almost all holding a PhD) and 200 non -academic staff, FCT NOVA's has

has earned recognition by its peers. 
FCT NOVA is organized in 14 Departments and 14 Research Support Services, with suitable structures,

of them as Exceptional and 4 as Excellent), spin -off incubator (Madan Parque), interface institute

PARTNER: 5- IPC 
Full name: IPC – Centre Technique Industriel 
de la Plasturgie et des Composites 
Web page: www.ct-ipc.com 
Country: France  
Type: RO 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
IPC is the Technical Industrial Centre of the French plastics and composites industry  cluster, with more 
than 3000 SMEs directly connected to IPC. As such, IPC is in charge of providing the plastics and 
composites industry cluster with innovative and high added value facilities and manufacturing pilot lines, 
cutting edge expertise and services. IPC covers the full industry value chain with its key fields of expertise 
including design and simulation of parts and processes; advanced injection moulding and tooling; 
thermoplastics materials; composites materials; plastronics (also known as 3D -MID, for Molded 
Interconnect Devices). Main markets addressed today encompass automotive, aeronautics, health, 
packaging, connectors, house appliances, horology. Developing new value chains is a key strategic issue 
with focus e. g. on micro / nanostructured  plastic parts, microsystems on plastics; smart composites; 
multi-materials additive manufacturing. 
Role in the Project:  
Within the NEMOSINE project, IPC will be in charge of developing the injection moulding -based process 
for the manufacturing of the mod ular multi -functional package for CH protection. This will more 
specifically include: 
- modular multi-functional package design  
- development of O2 barrier films (material development, extrusion/calendaring, characterization)

PARTNER: 6 - PROM 
Full name: Promethean Particles Ltd. 
Web page : 
www.prometheanparticles.co.uk 
Country: UK 
Type: SME 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
Promethean Particles (PROM) is a UK -based SME that designs and develops inorganic nanomaterials in 
liquid dispersions.  The company technology is based on a patented reactor system that allows truly 
continuous hydrothermal synthesis of inorganic nanoparticles for the first time (patent WO2005077505).  
PROM design and develop inorganic nanoparticle dispersions for industrial customers and then 
manufacture commercial quantities at our pilot plant.  Our unique productio n process allows us to tailor 
the nanoparticles to get the best functionality for an end use application. 
Role in the Project:  
PROM will be responsible for the upscaling of MOF synthesis during the project. PROM has the ability to 
synthesise a range of MO Fs in different compositions and this has been demonstrated at multi -kg scale 
using their one -step continuous manufacturing route. PROM will have significant input into the selection 
of MOF materials that will be upscaled using the continuous flow approach . PROM will advise and co -
ordinate with consortium partners in WP1 to develop the most appropriate MOF syntheses at lab-scale.  
Scientific team:  
Dr Pete Gooden (M)  is the Technical Manager at PROM.  He has an MSci degree and PhD in Chemistry 
from the Uni versity of Nottingham.  He specialised in high pressure and temperature synthesis for this 
research work.  Pete joined PROM in 2009 and as Technical Manager now oversees all technical work 
undertaken at PROM.  This includes the design and synthesis of new inorganic nanoparticle dispersions 
and industrial scale manufacture of these materials. Pete will co -ordinate the scientific activities within 
this project on behalf of PROM.

Technical equipment:  
PROM possesses lab-scale reactors capable of screening and producing small batches (g/hr throughput of 
dry weight equivalent) of nanomaterials. PROM also ow ns a pilot-scale reactor system (mentioned above) 
which is capable of producing kg scale quantities per day. This reactor system is housed at PROM’s 
facilities in Nottingham. 
PROM operates a full-scale continuous reactor system capable of producing up to 1000 tonnes per year of 
nanomaterials.

PARTNER: 8 - 
BIOSENSOR 
Full name : BIOSENSOR 
SRL 
Web page : 
http://www.biosensor-
srl.eu/ 
Country: ITALY 
Type: SME 
 
Brief description of the organization:  Biosensor is a SME at limited responsibility  founded in 2003. 
Biosensor works in the field of production and commercialization of sensors and biosensors. Most of 
Biosensor’s production is focus on the design, fabrication and product engineering of miniaturized modular 
portable instruments suitable for a variety of applications, especially for environmental applications.  
The devices use optical, amperometric, impedimetric  transduction modules to detect the signal generated 
by  organic porphyrins, polymers,  proteins, enzymes, bacteria, cells, RNA, D NA marked with fluorescent 
probes and/ or inorganic nanostructured materials (ZnO). The receptor material is immobilized on various 
inorganic-organic materials microelectrodes, microelectrodes array, screen printed electrodes, glasses 
coated with indium -tin oxide, graphene microelectrodes etc.  In the last years to enhance the ability to 
sense, detect, analyze, monitor and act on phenomena on nano scale (as for the presence of biomedical 
markers at lower fM levels), nanoparticles were used for the immobiliz ation of the biomaterials, for 
example, quantum dots integrated with magnetic beads. 
It has produced sensors for Space research for various research institutions, tested in ESA flights and at 
International Space Station from 2000 -2007; another flight to IS S is expected in 2018 
http://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/station/research/experiments/804.html 
It has developed detection techniques based on lasers, LEDs, photodiodes a nd different types of filters 
with disposable screen -printed electrodes, nanowires, planar microelectrode arrays, ITO coated -glasses 
etc. The base concept of all Biosensor’s devices is the production of portable low size and weight, 
multifunction systems capable of integrating the unique detection characteristics of the biomediators (high 
sensitivity, specificity, reproducibility of analysis, rapidity, simple use and low cost) with the necessary 
mechanical, electronic and microfluidic parts for automatic me asurements. The sensors are also provided 
of ICT applications for large data analyses in specific applications such as environmental monitoring and 
control. The on -board processing also includes analysis of sensor data to determine if certain thresholds 
are reached, generating an appropriate action, such as raising an alarm or increasing measuring frequency, 
and interfaces with the storage subcomponent to write/read sensor data from a database. It makes 
biosensor services accessible remotely, such as system  update, system configuration (e.g., sensor 
measuring frequency), sensor data queries. 
Role in the Project: Biosensor Srl will be involved in the following activities: 
-fabrication of sensitive layers for detection of low concentrations of O2, NO and aceti c acids, based on 
ZnO nanorods, porphyrine, conductive polymer and hybrid ZnO Nanorods/organic compound 
nanostructures. 
-Sensitivity tests to the target gas/vapours under different analyte concentrations, relative humidity and 
ambient temperatures, using p hotoluminescence/fluorescence, photocurrent and absorption 
spectroscopy. 
-Sensitivity and selectivity analysis, cross sensitivity measurements and optimization of sensor elements. 
-Development of an integrated compact multisensor system with portable excit ation light sources (LEDs) 
and optical detector systems (photodiodes, CCD matrixes). 
-Development of algorithms of sensitivity analysis for integration with wireless communication system. 
-Preliminary pilot plan analysis for production, Market analyses, exploitation and dissemination.

PARTNER 10 - NPH 
Full name: Nanopharma, a.s. 
Web page: www.nanopharma.cz 
Country: Czech Republic 
Type: SME 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
Nanopharma, a.s. is a Czech -based technology SME operating in the area of nanomaterials engineering. 
Founded in 2008, the company started developing reproducible and scalable electrospinning technologies 
for preparation of biocompatible nanofiber -based materials. Later on, the company started developing 
nanofiber-based applicati ons f or biomedicine, but also other industrial areas such as agriculture, textile, 
cosmetics, food, packaging, and many others. Apart from developing and commercializing its own material 
portfolio, Nanopharma carries out R&D contracts for industrial and re search partners interested in using 
nanofibers for their innovation projects.  
The company is very active in conducting more material research through the Nanoprogres nanotechnology 
cluster and international research projects, e.g. FP7. 
Role in the Project:  
Nanopharma will be responsible for the preparation of nanofibrous carriers with controlled release kinetics 
of incorporated MOFs an d antifungals. Different techniques will be used to achieve these goals, namely 
classic electrospinning, coaxial electrosp inning and nano -encapsulation. Nanopharma will be also 
responsible for evaluation of the nanostructured materials produced throughout the project activity by 
using several standard analytical methods, e.g. EDS, SEM. 
Nanopharma will also participate in the scale-up process of laboratory products created for various 
applications and in dissemination and exploitation of results.

research and development programs and she is also responsible for  coordination of national and 
international research projects.  Katerina will co -ordinate the scientific activities, lead full time and timely 
execution of the proposed work plan and on -going controlling and risk analysis within this project on behalf

PARTNER 13 - OEAW 
Full name : Oesterreichische Akademie der 
Wissenschaften - Phonogrammarchiv 
Web page: www.phonogrammarchiv.at, 
www.oeaw.ac.at 
Country: Austria 
Type:  
 
Brief description of the organization : The Austrian Academy of Sciences (OeAW)  is Austria’s central non-
university research and science institution. Founded in 1847 as a learned society, today the OeAW has over 
770 members and 1,450 employees dedicated to innovative basic research, interdisciplinary exchange of 
knowledge and the dissemination of new ins ights with the aim of contributing to progress in science and 
society as a whole.  The OeAW operates 28 research institutes in the field of innovative basic research in 
the arts and humanities and the social and natural sciences. The Academy stimulates pion eering research 
by taking up future-oriented topics and ensuring the preservation and interpretation of cultural heritage. 
The designated project partner Phonogrammarchiv, an institute of the Austrian Academy of Sciences, was 
founded in 1899 and is the old est audiovisual research archive in the world. From the very beginnings it 
has aimed to produce, collec t, preserve and make accessible sound recordings as acoustical sources for all 
disciplines concerned, without regional restrictions. Its holdings consist  almost exclusively of field 
recordings, made chiefly by Austrian scholars and comprising ethnomusicolo gy, (ethno -) linguistics and 
cultural anthropology.  
Today the Phonogrammarchiv holds ca. 75.000 items of recorded sound and video material, both analogue 
and digital. As a result of the great variety of different formats in its holdings, the Phonogrammarc hiv has 
developed internationally acclaimed expertise in long time storage, preservation, restoration, transfer and 
digitisation of audio.  
In 1999, UNES CO included the archive’s historical collections (1899 –1950) as documents of universal 
significance in the World Register of its “Memory of the World” Programme; and in 2007 the 
Phonogrammarchiv received the UNESCO/Jikji Memory of the World Prize, the highest international award 
for significant contributions to the preservation of documentary heritage. Addi tionally, the 
Phonogrammarchiv is part of the Austrian CLARIN consortium (digital humanities research infrastructure 
consortium), https://www.clarin.eu/node/4199.  
The Phonogrammarchiv has a wide experience in the storage, restoration, transfer and treatme nt of 
cellulose acetate based materials and has carried out substantial research in this field. The 
Phonogrammarchiv of the Austrian Academy of Sciences,  Vienna, has together with the Austrian Institute 
for Chemistry and Technology OFI, developed a method to permanently refresh acetate media, especially 
those affected by the chemical deterioration process referred to as “vinegar syndrome”. 
The method has been patented (Pub. No.: WO/2012/088553), and an exclusive licensing contract has been 
made with the com mercial company NOA GmbH. As part of a public -private-partnership, the restoration 
process is in further development for industrial applications, as well  as in verification, in cooperation with 
NOA GmbH Vienna and consultants of the University of Vienna, I nstitute for Organic Chemistry, Univ. Prof. 
Dr. Erich Schmid. 
Role in the Project:

collections, related input on package design criteria. WP7: Materials evalua tion: validation of package 
design and efficacy (acidity testing, accelerated ageing, functionality, applicability, audiovisual signal 
quality evaluation). WP9: Contribution to business model, communication and dissemination (participation 
in industry-lead events related to cultural heritage artefacts, networking within audiovisual communities & 
heritage institutions as well as their umbrella organisations, e.g. IASA, AES, UNESCO).
